"GOD WILL LOOK AFTER A POOR DEVIL LIKE ME."

"Mr. President," she cried over the heads of the others, "this letter is not in Mr. Rossi's handwriting. It is a forgery. I am ready to prove it."

"總統先生，"她的哭喊聲穿過眾人，"這封信不是Rossi先生的筆跡。這是偽造的。我已準備好證明它。"

At that moment one of the Carabineers came back to tell the judges that all was over.

就在那一刻，其中一名卡拉賓槍手回來向法官報告，一切都已經結束了。

"Gone!" said one after another, more often with a motion of the mouth than with the voice.

"一個接一個地說：“走了！”這話經常是以口型，而不是聲音形式表達出來。"

The president was deeply agitated. "This court stands adjourned," he said, "but I take the Almighty to witness that I intend to ascertain all responsibility in this case and to bring it home to the guilty ones, whosoever and whatsoever they may be."

總統非常不安。他說：“本法庭現在休庭，但我要向全能的上帝保證，我打算查明這個案子的所有責任並歸咎於有罪的人，無論他們可能是誰或是什麼。”

XVIII

"My dear David Rossi,—You will know all about it before this letter reaches you. It is one of those scandals of the law that are telegraphed to every part of the civilised world. Poor Bruno! Yet no, not poor—great, glorious, heroic Bruno! He ended like an old Roman, and killed himself rather than betray his friend. When they played upon his jealousy, and tempted him by a forged letter, he cried, 'Long live David Rossi!' and died. Oh, it was wonderful. The memory of that moment will be with me always like the protecting and strengthening hand of God. I never knew until to-day what human nature is capable of. It is divine.

"親愛的大衛·羅西，你在這封信到達你之前，就會知道所有的事情。這是法律的醜聞之一，被電報傳遍整個文明世界。可憐的布魯諾！不，不是可憐—偉大，光榮，英勇的布魯諾！他像一個古羅馬人一樣結束了生命，寧願自殺也不背叛他的朋友。當他們利用他的嫉妒心，並用一封偽造的信誘惑他時，他喊出：'大衛·羅西萬歲！'然後就死了。哦，這真是驚人。那一刻的回憶將一直伴隨我，就像上帝的保護和強化的手。直到今天，我才知道人類的本性有多神聖。"

"But how mean and little I feel when I think of all I went through in the court this morning! I was really undergoing the same tortures as Bruno, the same doubt and the same agony. And even when I saw through the whole miserable machination of lying and duplicity I was actually in terror for Bruno lest he should betray you in the end. Betray you! His voice when he uttered that last cry rings in my ears still. It was a voice of triumph—triumph over deception, over temptation, over jealousy, and over self.

"但是，當我想到今天早上在法庭上所經歷的一切時，我覺得自己如此卑微與渺小！我真的和Bruno一樣，在經歷著同樣的痛苦、相同的疑惑和同樣的痛苦。即使我看透了整個悲慘的謊言與偽善的陰謀，我實際上仍對Bruno感到恐慌，擔心他到最後可能會背叛你。背叛你！他那最後一句哭喊的聲音還在我耳邊回響。那是一種戰勝欺騙、誘惑、嫉妒和自我的勝利之聲。"

"Don't think, David Rossi, that Bruno died of a broken heart, and don't think he went out of the world believing that you were false. I feel sure he came to that court with the full intention of doing what he did. All through the trial there was something in his bearing which left the impression of a purpose unrevealed. Everybody felt it, and even the judges ceased to protest against his outbursts. The poor prisoner in convict clothes, with dishevelled hair and bare neck, made every one else look paltry and small. Behind him was something mightier than himself. It was Death. Then remember his last cry, and ask yourself what he meant by it. He meant loyalty, love, faith, fidelity. He intended to say, 'You've beaten me, but no matter; I believe in him, and follow him to the last.'

"不要以為，大衛·羅西，布魯諾是由於心碎而死，也不要以為他離世的時候認為你是虛偽的。我確信他來到那個法庭，全心全意的想要做他所做的事。在整個審判過程中，他的態度中有些東西給人留下了一種未揭示的目的的印象。每個人都感覺到了，甚至法官也停止了對他的爆發的抗議。可憐的囚犯，穿著囚衣，頭髮凌亂，脖子赤裸裸的，使每個人都顯得微不足道。他身後的東西比他本人還要偉大。那就是死亡。然後記住他最後的呼喊，問問自己他的意思是什麼。他的意思是忠誠，愛，信仰，忠實。他想要說，'你們打敗了我，但沒關系；我相信他，並追隨他到底。'"

"As you see, I am here in your own quarters, but I keep in touch with 'Sister Angelica,' and still have no answer to my letter. I invent all manner of excuses to account for your silence. You are busy, you are on a journey, you are waiting for the right moment to reply to me at length. If I could only continue to think so, how happy I should be! But I cannot deceive myself any longer.

"如你所見，我在你的空間裡，但我還是與'安潔莉卡修女'保持聯繫，卻仍然無法得到我信函的答覆。我編造各種藉口為你的沉默找理由。你忙，你在旅途中，你在等待適合的時候詳細回答我。如果我能繼續這樣想，我將會多麼快樂！但我再也不能欺騙自己了。"

"It is perhaps natural that you should find it hard to forgive me, but you might at least write and put me out of suspense. I think you would do so if you knew how much I suffer. Your great soul cannot intend to torture me. To-night the burden of things is almost more than I can bear, and I am nearly heartbroken. It is my dark hour, dearest, and if you had to say you could never forgive me, I think I could easier reconcile myself to that. I have been so happy since I began to love you; I shall always love you even if I have to lose you, and I shall never, never be sorry for anything that has occurred.

"也許你發現原諒我很困難是自然的，但你至少可以寫信讓我擺脫掛念。我想如果你知道我有多痛苦，你會這麼做的。你的偉大靈魂不可能意圖折磨我。今晚，事情的重擔幾乎讓我無法承受，我幾乎心碎。這是我最黑暗的時刻，親愛的，即使你說你永遠無法原諒我，我想我也能更輕易地接受。自從開始愛你以來，我一直很快樂；即使我必須失去你，我仍然會一直愛你，而且我永遠，永遠不會對發生的事情感到遺憾。"

"Not receiving any new letters from you, I am going back on the old ones, and there is a letter of only two months ago in which you speak of just such a case as mine. May I quote what you say?

"我沒有收到你的新信，所以我在重讀舊信中。其中有一封只有兩個月的信，你在信中提到了一個和我現在情況相似的案例。我可以引用你說的話嗎？"

"'Yet even if she were not so (i.e. worthy of your love and friendship), even if there were, as you say, a fault in her, who am I that I should judge her harshly? ... I reject the monstrous theory that while a man may redeem the past a woman never can.... And if she has sinned as I have sinned, and suffered as I have suffered, I will pray for strength to say, 'Because I love her we are one, and we stand or fall together.'

"`即使她不是如此（即，值得你的愛和友誼），即使她真的如你所說，有所過錯，我又有什麼資格嚴厲地去評判她呢？...我完全否定那種怪誕的理著，認為男人可以挽回過去，而女人卻永遠不能...。如果她像我一樣犯了錯，像我一樣受過苦，我會祈禱給我力量說，‘因為我愛她，我們是一體的，我們一起立下或一起墮落。'"

"It is so beautiful that I am even happy while my pen copies the sweet, sweet words, and I feel as I did when the old priest spoke so tenderly on the day I confessed, telling me I had committed no sin and had nothing to repent of. Have I never told you about that? My confessor was a Capuchin, and perhaps I should have waited for his advice before going farther. He was to consult his General or his Bishop or some one, and to send for me again.

"這是如此美麗，以至於我在抄寫這些甜蜜的，甜蜜的詞句時甚至感到快樂，我感覺就像在我告解的那天，老神父如此溫柔地說話時一樣，他告訴我我並未犯下任何罪孽，也無需懺悔。我有沒有告訴過你關於那個的？我的神父是個門脂會修士，也許在走得更遠之前，我應該等待他的意見。他要去諮詢他的將軍或主教還是某人，然後再來找我。"

"But all that is over now, and everything depends upon you. In any case, be sure of one thing, whatever happens. Bruno has taught me a great lesson, and there is not anything your enemies can do to me that will touch me now. They have tried me already with humiliation, with poverty, with jealousy, and even with the shadow of shame itself. There is nothing left but death. And death itself shall find me faithful to the last. Good-bye! Your poor unforgiven girl,

"但是，所有那些都已經結束了，一切都取決於你。無論如何，請確定一件事，不管發生什麼。布魯諾已經教給我一個重大的教訓，現在你的敵人再也不能對我做什麼能夠觸及我的事情了。他們已經用羞辱、貧窮，甚至羨慕和恥辱的陰影試探過我。只剩下死亡。而死亡也將發現我忠誠到底。再見！你可憐的，未被原諒的女孩，"

Roma."

羅馬

The morning after writing this letter Roma received a visit from one of the Noble Guard. It was the Count de Raymond.

在寫完這封信的第二天早上，羅馬接到了一位貴族衛士的來訪。那是雷蒙德伯爵。

"I am sent by the Holy Father," he said, "to say that he wishes to see you."

"我是由聖父派來的,"他說,"他希望見你。"

PART SEVEN—THE POPE

I

On the morning appointed for the visit to the Vatican, Roma dressed in the black gown and veil prescribed by etiquette for ladies going to an audience with the Pope.

約定參觀梵蒂岡的那個早晨，羅馬穿上了被禮節規定的黑色禮服和面紗，準備去見教宗。

The young Noble Guard in civilian clothes was waiting for her in the sitting-room. When she came out of the bedroom he was standing with a solemn face before the bust of David Rossi, which she had lately cast afresh and was beginning to point in marble.

一名年輕的貴族衛士穿著便服，在客廳等待著她。當她從臥室出來時，他正嚴肅地站在大衛·羅西的半身像前，她最近重新鑄造了這個半身像，並開始用大理石精雕細琢。

"This is wonderful," he said. "Perfectly wonderful! A most astonishing study."

"這真是太棒了，"他說。"簡直太棒了！這是一個最令人驚訝的研究。"

Roma smiled and bowed to him.

羅馬向他微笑並鞠躬。

"Christ of course, and such reality, such feeling, such love! But shall I tell you what surprises me most of all?"

"基督當然，還有那樣的現實，那樣的感情，那樣的愛！但是我應該告訴您最讓我驚訝的事情嗎？"

"What?"

"什麼？"

"What surprises me most is the extraordinary resemblance between your Christ and the Pope."

"令我最驚訝的是，你們的基督和教皇之間的非凡相似性。"

"Really?"

"真的嗎？"

"Indeed yes! Didn't you know it? No? It is almost incredible. Younger certainly, but the same features, the same expression, the same tenderness, the same strength! Even the same vertical lines over the nose which make the shako dither on one's head when something goes wrong and His Holiness is indignant."

"確實如此！你難道不知道嗎？還真不知道嗎？這幾乎是不可思議。雖然更年輕，但具有相同的面部特徵，相同的表情，相同的溫柔，相同的力量！甚至那些在鼻樑上的垂直線條也相同，它們在出現困難，並且教宗憤怒時，會讓軍帽在頭上晃動。"

Roma's smile was dying off her face like the sun off a field of corn, and she was looking sideways out of the window.

"羅馬的笑容就像陽光從玉米田中消逝一樣,開始從她臉上褪去。她正側著臉看窗外。"

"Has the Pope any relations?" she asked.

"教宗有任何親戚嗎？"

"None whatever, not a soul. The only son of an only son. You must have been thinking of the Holy Father himself, and asking yourself what he was like thirty years ago. Come now, confess it!"

"一點都沒有，一點都沒有。唯一的兒子的唯一的兒子。您一定是想起了教宗本人，並問自己他三十年前是什麼樣的。來吧，承認吧!"

Roma laughed. The soldier laughed. "Shall we go?" she said.

羅馬笑了。士兵也笑了。“我們走吧？”她說。

A carriage was waiting for them, and they drove by the Tor di Nona, a narrow lane which skirts the banks of the Tiber, across the bridge of St. Angelo, and up the Borgo.

他們有一輛馬車在等候，他們經過托爾迪諾納，這是一條沿著台伯河岸的狹窄小巷，越過聖安祖洛橋，然後向上走到博戈。

Roma was nervous and preoccupied. Why had she been sent for? What could the Pope have to say to her?

"羅馬緊張且心事重重。為什麼她被召喚？教皇會跟她說些什麼呢？"

"Isn't it unusual," she asked, "for the Pope to send for any one—especially a woman, and a non-Catholic?"

"難道不奇怪嗎?"她問，"教皇會傳召任何人——尤其是一個女人，而且還不是天主教徒嗎?"

"Most unusual. But perhaps Father Pifferi...."

"最不尋常。 但也許Pifferi神父...."

"Father Pifferi?"

"父親皮費瑞？"

"He is the Holy Father's confessor."

"他是教宗的告解師。"

"Is he a Capuchin?"

"他是閣布津嗎？"

"Yes. The General at San Lorenzo."

"是的。位於聖洛倫索的將軍。"

"Ah, now I understand," said Roma. Light had dawned on her and her spirits began to rise.

"啊，現在我明白了，"羅馬說。她開始理解，她的精神開始振作起來。

"The Pope is very tender and fatherly, isn't he?"

"教皇非常和藹且像父親般的，不是嗎？"

"Fatherly? He is a saint on earth, that's what he is! Impetuous, perhaps, but so sweet and generous and forgiving. Makes you shake in your shoes if you've done anything amiss, but when all is over and he puts his arm on your shoulder and tells you to think no more about it, you're ready to die for him even at the stake."

"父親般的？他就是地球上的聖人！也許衝動，但非常甜蜜、慷慨和寬恕。如果你做錯了什麼，他會讓你害怕得發抖。但當一切結束，他將手臂放在你的肩膀上，告訴你不再想它，你會願意甚至在火刑柱上為他犧牲自己。"

Roma's spirits were rising every minute, and her nervousness was fading away. Since things had fallen out so, she could take advantage of her opportunities. She would tell the Pope everything, and he would advise with her and counsel her. She would speak about David Rossi, and the Pope would tell her what to do.

羅馬的精神每分鐘都在提升，她的緊張情緒也在消退。既然事情已經發生了，她可以利用自己的機會。她將把所有事情告訴教皇，他會對她進行指導和勸告。她會提起大衛·羅西，教皇會告訴她該怎麼做。

The great clock of the Basilica was striking ten with a solemn boom as the carriage rattled over the stones of the Piazza of St. Peter's—wet with the play of the fountains and bright with the rainbows made by the sun.

當大教堂的大鐘以莊嚴的轟響敲擊十下時，馬車在聖彼得廣場的石頭上嘎嘎作響 - 噴泉的水花四濺，陽光製造出燦爛的彩虹。

They alighted at the bronze gate, ascended the grand staircase, crossed a courtyard, passed through many gorgeous chambers, and arrived finally at an apartment hung with tapestries and occupied by a Noble Guard, who wore a brass helmet and held a drawn sword. The next room was the throne room, and beyond it were the Pope's private apartments.

他們在銅門下車，上了宏偉的樓梯，穿過了一個庭院，經過了許多華麗的房間，最後來到了一個掛著掛毯的公寓，由一個貴族護衛住宿，他戴著一個黃銅頭盔並拿著一把劍。 下一個房間是皇室，而且它後面是教宗的私人公寓。

A chaplain of the Pope's household came to say that by request of Father Pifferi the lady was to step into an anteroom; and Roma followed him into a small adjoining chamber, carpeted with cocoanut matting and furnished with a marble-topped table and two wooden chest-seats, bearing the papal arms. The little room opened on to a corridor overlooking a courtyard, a secret way to the Pope's private rooms, and it had a door to the throne room also.

教皇的牧師來傳達一個消息，根據Pifferi神父的要求，這位女士應進入一個側廳，於是Roma跟隨他走進了一個小房間。該房間用椰子毯子鋪就，配有一張大理石頂桌子和兩個木製箱形座位，上面有教皇的徽章。這個小房間通向俯瞰庭院的走廊，這是通往教皇私人房間的秘密路徑，它也有一扇通往王座室的門。

"The Father will be here presently," said the chaplain, "and His Holiness will not be long."

"將會有神父來到這裡，" 牧師說， "他的聖潔也不會久等。"

Roma, who was feeling some natural tremors, tried to reassure herself by asking questions about the Pope. The chaplain's face began to gleam. He was a little man, with round red cheeks and pale grey eyes, and the usual tone of his voice was a hushed and reverent whisper.

"羅馬, 她感覺到一些天然的震顫, 試圖透過詢問有關教皇的問題來安撫自己。牧師的臉開始發光。他是一個小個子男人，有著圓圓的紅臉頰和蒼白的灰色眼睛，他的聲音通常是低聲而恭敬的耳語。"

"Faint? Yes, ladies do faint sometimes—often, I may say—and they nearly always cry. But the Holy Father is so gentle, so sweet."

"昏厥？是的，有時候女士們會昏厥-我可以說經常，她們幾乎總是會哭泣。但是聖父是如此的溫柔，如此的甜美。"

The door to the throne room opened and there was a gleam of violet and an indistinct buzz of voices. The chaplain disappeared, and at the next moment a man in the dress of a waiter came from the corridor carrying a silver soup dish.

皇位室的門開啟了，洋溢出一股紫羅蘭的光芒和模糊的談話聲。牧師消失了，下一刻，一個穿著侍者服裝的男子從走廊走出，手裡拿著一個銀湯碗。

"You're the lady the Holy Father sent for?"

"您就是教宗召見的那位女士嗎？"

Roma smiled and assented.

洛馬微笑並同意。

"I'm Cortis—Gaetano Cortis—the Pope's valet, you know—and of course I hear everything."

「我是科提斯 - 蓋塔諾科提斯 - 你知道的，教皇的僕人，我當然聽到了一切。」

Roma smiled again and bowed.

羅馬再次微笑並鞠躬。

"I bring the Holy Father a plate of soup every morning at ten, but I'm afraid it is going to get cold this morning."

"我每天早上十點給教宗帶一盤湯，但我擔心今天早上會變冷。"

"Will he be angry?"

“他會生氣嗎？”

"Angry? He's an angel, and couldn't be angry with any one."

"生氣？他是天使，不可能對任何人生氣。"

"He must indeed be good; everybody says so."

"他確實一定很好; 每個人都這麼說。"

"He is perfect. That's about the size of it. None of your locking up his bedroom when he goes into the garden and putting the key into the pocket of his cassock, same as in the old Pope's days. I go in whenever I like, and he lets me take whatever I please. At Christmas some rich Americans wanted a skull-cap to save a dying man, and I got it for the asking. Now an old English lady wants a stocking to cure her rheumatism, and I'll get that too. I've saved a little hair from the last cutting, and if you hear of anybody...."

"他就是完美的化身。就是這樣。他並不像舊時的教皇那樣，出門到花園的時候鎖起自己的臥室，然後將鑰匙放入長袍的口袋。我隨時都可以進去，他讓我任意取用。在聖誕節時，一些有錢的美國人想要一頂髮冠來拯救一個瀕死的人，我只需一句話就得到了。現在，一位老年的英國女士想要一隻襪子來治療她的風濕病，我也將得到。上一次剪髮時我保存了一些頭髮，如果你聽到有人需要..."

The valet's story of his perquisites was interrupted by the opening of the door of the throne room and the entrance of a friar in a brown habit. It was Father Pifferi.

`僕人關於他的特權的故事被寶座房間的門開啟以及一位穿著棕色僧袍的修士的進入所打斷。那是Pifferi神父。`

"Don't rise, my daughter," he said, and closing the door behind the valet, he gathered up the skirts of his habit and sat down on the chest-seat in front of her.

"別起來，我的女兒，"他說，並在僕人關上門後，他撩起自己衣服的裙子，坐在她面前的箱子座位上。

"When you came to me with your confidence, my child, and I found it difficult to advise with you for your peace of mind, I told you I wished to take your case to a wiser head than mine. I took it to the Pope himself. He was touched by your story, and asked to see you for himself."

"當你帶著自信來找我，我的孩子，我發現要給你心靈的平靜提供建議有些困難，我告訴你我希望將你的情況帶給比我更有智慧的人。我把它帶給了教皇本人。他被你的故事所打動，並要求親自見你。"

"But, Father...."

"但是，父親...."

"Don't be afraid, my daughter. Pius the Tenth as a Pope may be lofty to sternness, but as a man he is humble and simple and kind. Forget that he is a sovereign and a pontiff, and think of him as a tender and loving friend. Tell him everything. Hold nothing back. And if you must needs reveal the confidences of others, remember that he is the Vicar of Him who keeps all our secrets."

"不要害怕，我的女兒。作為教皇的庇護十世可能威嚴至極，但作為一個人，他卻是謙遜、單純和仁慈的。請你忘記他是一個統治者和教皇，想他只是一個溫柔且愛你的朋友。傾訴給他所有的事情，不要有任何保留。即使你必須揭示他人的秘密，也要記住他是那位保護我們所有秘密的神的代理人。"

"But, Father...."

"但是，爸爸...."

"Yes."

"是的。"

"He is so high, so holy, so far above the world and its temptations...."

"他是如此崇高，如此神聖，遠在世界及其誘惑之上...."

"Don't say that, my daughter. The Holy Father is a man like other men. Shall I tell you something of his life? The world knows it only by hearsay and report. You shall hear the truth, and when you have heard it you will go to him as a child goes to its father, and no longer be afraid."

"別這樣說，我的女兒。教皇也是一個人。我該告訴你一些他的生活故事嗎？世界只是以聞說和報導的方式知道他的事。你將聽到真相，當你瞭解後，你會像一個孩子去找她的父親，而不再害怕。"

II

"Thirty-five years ago," said Father Pifferi, "the Holy Father had not even dreamt of being Pope. He was the only child of a Roman banker, living in a palace on the opposite side of the piazza. The old Baron had visions, indeed, of making his son a great churchman by the power of wealth, but these were vain and foolish, and the young man did not share them. His own aims were simple but worldly. He desired to be a soldier, and to compromise with his father's disappointed ambitions he asked for a commission in the Pope's Noble Guard."

"三十五年前，"皮菲里神父說，"當時的教宗還沒有做教宗的夢。他是一個羅馬銀行家的獨生子，在廣場對面的一座宮殿中生活。老男爵確實有幻想利用財富使他的兒子成為一位大教士，但這些都是徒然和愚蠢的，年輕人並不與之共鳴。他自己的目標很簡單但世俗。他渴望成為一位士兵，為了滿足父親失望的期待，他竟然求就教宗的貴族衛隊的職位。"

The old friar put his hands into the vertical pockets in the breast of his habit, and looked up at the ceiling as he went on speaking.

那位老僧侶將手插進他僧袍胸前的直立口袋裡，繼續說話時抬頭看著天花板。

"All this is no secret, but what follows is less known. The soldier, who had the charm of an engaging personality, led the life of an ordinary young Roman of his day, frequenting cafés, concerts, theatres, and balls. In this character he met a poor woman of the people, and came to love her. She was a good girl, with soft and gentle manners, but a heart of gold and a soul of fire. He was a good man and he meant to marry her. He did marry her. He married her according to the rites of the Church, which are all that religion requires and God calls for."

"這些都不是秘密，但隨後的情況就較少人知道。那名士兵具有吸引人的個性魅力，他過著一個普通的年輕羅馬人的生活，常常去咖啡館，音樂會，劇院和舞會。在這樣的角色中，他遇到了一個窮苦的平民女子，並愛上了她。她是個好女孩，態度溫柔且友善，但她有一顆黃金般的心和炙熱如火的靈魂。他是好人，他打算娶她。他確實娶了她。他按照教堂的儀式娶了她，這是宗教所要求的所有事物，也是上帝的呼召。"

Roma was leaning forward on her seat and breathing between tightly-closed lips.

"羅馬正前傾在她的座位上，並且緊緊閉著嘴唇進行呼吸。"

"Unhappily, then as now, a godless legislature had separated a religious from a civil marriage, and the one without the other was useless. The old Baron heard of what had happened and tried to defeat it. A cardinal had just been created in Australia, and an officer of the Noble Guard had to be sent with the Ablegate to carry the biglietto and the skull-cap. At the request of the Baron his son was appointed to that mission and despatched in haste."

"不幸的是，就像現在一樣，一個無神論的立法機關將宗教婚姻與民事婚姻分開，缺一不可。老男爵聽說了這件事，試圖阻止。澳洲剛創立了一位樞機主教，一位貴族衛隊的軍官必須與該樞機主教一同送去告知書和樞機主教的帽子。應男爵的要求，他的兒子被任命為該任務的負責人，並被迅速派遣出去。"

Roma could scarcely control herself.

"羅馬幾乎無法控制自己。"

"The young husband being gone, the father set himself to deal with the wife. He had not yet relinquished his hopes of seeing his son a churchman, and marriage was a fatal impediment. A rich man may have many instruments, and the Baron was able to use some that were evil. He played upon the conscience of the girl, who was pure and virtuous; told her she was not legally married, and that the laws of her country thought ill of her. Finally, he appealed to her love for her husband, and showed her that she was standing in his way. He was not a bad man, but he loved his son beyond truth and to the perversion of honour, and was ready to sacrifice the woman who stood between them. She allowed herself to be sacrificed. She wiped herself out that she might not be an obstacle to her husband. She drowned herself in the Tiber."

"年輕的丈夫離開之後，父親便開始與妻子打交道。他仍未放棄希望看到自己的兒子成為教士，而婚姻卻是一個致命的障礙。富有的人可能有許多工具，男爵能夠利用其中一些惡劣的手段。他影響了那位純潔、有道德的女孩的良知，告訴她她並未合法結婚，她的國家的法律對她有不良的評價。最後，他呼籲她對丈夫的愛，告訴她她正在阻礙丈夫的道路。他並不是一個壞人，但他熱愛他的兒子超越了真理，甚至以女人的名譽為代價，願意犧牲那位站在他們之間的女人。她准許自己被犧牲。她為了不成為她丈夫的阻礙，選擇自我消滅。她在台伯河中投身自盡。"

Roma could not control herself any longer, and made a half-stifled exclamation.

"羅馬再也無法控制自己，發出了半壓抑的驚叫。"

"Then the young husband returned. He had been travelling constantly, and no letters from his wife had reached him. But one letter was waiting for him at Rome, and it told him what she had done. It was then all over; there was no help for it, and he was overwhelmed with horror. He could not blame the poor dead girl, for all she had done had been done in love; he could not blame himself, for he had meant no wrong in making the religious marriage, and had hastened home to complete the civil one; and he could not reproach his father, for if the Baron's conduct had led to fearful consequences, it had been prompted by affection for himself. But the hand of God seemed to be over him, and his soul was shaken to its foundations. From that time forward he renounced society and all worldly pleasures. For eight days he went into retreat and prayed fervently. On the ninth day he joined a religious house, the Novitiate of the Capuchins at San Lorenzo. The young soldier, so gay, so handsome, so fond of social admiration, became a friar."

然後，年輕的丈夫回來了。他一直在旅行，沒有收到來自他妻子的任何信件。但羅馬有一封信等著他，告訴他她所做的事。那時一切都結束了，無法再挽救，他被恐懼所淹沒。他不怪那個窮困的死去的女孩，因為她所做的一切都是出於愛；他不能責怪自己，因為他在進行宗教婚禮時並沒有想做錯事，而且他也洗帶著回家完成民事婚禮；他也不能責怪他的父親，因為如果男爵的行為導致了可怕的後果，那也是出於對他自己的愛。但上帝的手似乎在他身上，他的靈魂深受震撼。從那時起，他放棄了社會和所有世俗的樂趣。八天內，他退隱並熱情祈禱。第九天，他加入了一個宗教房屋，位於聖洛倫索的卡普奇諾修會新進修士。那位曾經如此快樂、英俊、如此喜歡社交讚美的年輕士兵變成了一名修道士。

The old Capuchin looked tenderly at Roma, whose wet eyes and burning cheeks seemed to tell of sympathy with his story.

那位老卡普奇諾僧依依不捨地看著羅馬，他那濕濕的眼睛和紅潤的臉頰似乎在流露對他故事的同情。

"In those days, my daughter, the nuns of Thecla served the Foundling of Santo Spirito."

在那些日子裡，我的女兒，忒克拉的修女們照顧著聖托斯皮里託的棄嬰。

Roma began to look frightened and to feel faint.

"羅馬開始看起來很害怕，感到有些暈眩。"

"It was usual for a member of our house to live in the hospital in order to baptize the children and to confess the sick and the dying. We took it in turns to do so, staying one year, two years, three years, and then going back to the monastery. I was myself at Santo Spirito for this purpose at the time I speak about, and it was not until three or four years afterwards that I became Superior of our House and returned to San Lorenzo. There I found the young Noble Guard, and, wisely or unwisely, I told him a new phase of his own story."

"我們家中的成員通常會住在醫院中，以對學生進行洗禮並給病人和臨終者作告解。我們輪流這樣做，留在那裡一年，兩年，三年，然後回到修道院。我在說這些事情的時候，我為了這個目的在Santo Spirito，直到三或四年後，我才成為我們家的主管並返回到San Lorenzo。在那裡，我找到了年輕的Noble Guard，不管是否明智，我都告訴他他自己故事的新階段。"

"There was a child?" said Roma, in a strange voice.

"有一個孩子嗎？" 羅馬用奇怪的聲音說。

The Capuchin bent his head. "That much he knew already by the letter his wife had left for him. She had intended that the child should die when she died, and he supposed that it had been so. But pity for the little one must have overtaken the poor mother at the last moment. She had put the babe in the rota of the hospital, and thus saved the child's life before carrying out her purpose upon her own."

卡布奇諾僧侶低下頭，"妻子遺留的信中已給予他這麼多的瞭解。她本打算自己死的時候讓孩子也隨之結束生命，他原本也以為事情就是這樣了。但應該是在最後一刻，對小孩的憐憫戰勝了這位可憐的母親。她把寶寶放在了醫院的嬰兒投放窗口，因此在對自己的生命做出決定前，她救了孩子的生命。"

The Capuchin crossed his knees, and one of his bare feet in its sandal showed from under the edge of his habit.

這名卡皮修林修道士交叉著膝蓋，他的一隻赤腳從長袍的邊緣露了出來，腳上只穿著一雙涼鞋。

"We had baptized the boy by a name which the mother had written on a paper attached to his wrist, and the identity of that name with the name of the Noble Guard led to my revelation. Nature is a mighty thing, and on hearing what I told him the young brother became restless and unhappy. The instincts of the man began to fight with the feelings of the religious, and at last he left the friary in order to fulfil the duty which he thought he owed to his child."

"我們已經根據母親在兒子手腕上附著的紙張所寫的名字，為這個男孩進行了洗禮，而這個名字與貴族衛隊的名字相同，這使我有了啟示。自然是一種偉大的力量，當我告訴他我們所發現的事情時，年輕的弟弟開始變得煩躁不安。人的本能開始和宗教的感情相抗衡，最後他決定離開修道院，以履行他認為欠缺的對他兒子的責任。"

"He did not find him?"

"他沒有找到他嗎？"

"He was too late. According to custom, the boy had been put out to nurse on the Campagna, by means of the little dower that was all his inheritance from the State. His foster parents passed him over to other hands, and thus by the abuse of a good practice the child was already lost."

"他已經來晚了。根據習俗，這個男孩被送到Campagna去撫養，這是他從國家繼承的一點點嫁妝。他的養父母將他移交給了其他人，因此，由於濫用良好的做法，這個孩子已經迷失了。"

Roma tried to speak, but she could not utter a word.

"羅馬試圖說話，但她無法發出一句話。"

"What happened then is a long story. The old Baron was now dead and the young friar had inherited his princely fortune. Dispensations got over canonical difficulties, and in due course he took holy orders. His first work was to establish in Rome an asylum for friendless orphans. He went out into the streets to look for them, and brought them in with his own hands. His fame for charity grew rapidly, and he knew well what he was doing. He was looking for the little fatherless one who owned his own blood and bore his name."

"然後發生的事情是一個長故事。老男爵現在已經去世，年輕的修道士繼承了他的王子般的財富。豁免規定解決了教會法律的困難，並且他適時地接受了聖職。他的第一項工作是在羅馬為無依無靠的孤兒建立一個收容所。他走進街頭去找他們，並親自把他們帶回來。他因慈善而迅速聞名，他知道自己在做什麼。他正在尋找那個擁有他自己血液，並帶著他名字的小孤兒。"

Roma was now sitting with drooping head, and her tears were falling on her hands.

羅馬現在低著頭坐著，她的淚水正在滴落在她的雙手上。

"Five years passed, and at length he came upon a trace of the boy and heard that he had been sent to England. The unhappy father obtained permission and removed to London. There he set up the same work as before and spent in the same way his great wealth. He passed five years more in a fruitless search, looking for his lost one day and night, winter and summer, in cold and heat, among the little foreign boys who play organs and accordions in the streets. Then he gave up hope and returned to Rome. His head was white and his heart was humble, but in spite of himself he rose from dignity to dignity until at length the old Baron's perverted ambitions were fulfilled. For his great and abounding charity, and still greater piety, he was promoted to be Bishop; seven years afterwards he was created Cardinal; and now he is Pope Pius the Tenth, the saint, the saviour of his people, once the storm-tossed, sorrowing, stricken man...."

"五年過去了，他終於找到了那個男孩的蹤跡，聽說他被送去了英格蘭。不幸的父親得到許可後，搬到了倫敦。在那裡，他開始了與之前相同的工作，並以同樣的方式花費他的巨額財富。他又用了五年的時間去尋找他失敗的孩子，無論白天還是黑夜，無論是寒冬還是炎夏，他都在在街頭彈著風琴和手風琴的小外國男孩中尋找他。然後他放棄了希望，回到了羅馬。他的頭髮已變成白色，他的心變得謙卑，但是他不得不從尊嚴中起身，直到最後滿足了老男爵的過分的野心。因為他的大量慈善行為和更大的虔誠，他被提升為主教；七年後，他被建立為樞機主教；現在他是教宗皮烏斯十世，一位聖人，一位拯救他的人民的救世主，曾經是一位風暴中的、悲傷的、被打擊的人...."

"David Leone?"

"大衛·利昂"

The Capuchin bowed. "That was the Holy Father's name. He committed no sin and has nothing to reproach himself with, but nevertheless he has known what it is to fall and to rise again, to suffer and be strong. Tell me, my daughter, is there anything you would be afraid to confide to him?"

"那位卡普奇林禮貌地鞠躬。"那是教皇的名字。他未犯過罪，也無需自我譴責，然而他明白什麼是起伏不定、承受痛苦並恢復堅強。告訴我，我女兒，有沒有什麼事情是你害怕向他透露的?"

"Nothing! Nothing whatever!" said Roma, with tears choking her voice and streaming down her cheeks.

"什麼也沒有！完全什麼也沒有！"羅馬說，聲音被淚水哽咽，眼淚順著她的臉頰流下來。

The door to the throne room opened again and a line of Cardinals came out and passed down the secret corridor, talking together as they walked, old men in violet, most of them very feeble and looking very tired. At the next moment the chaplain came in for Roma.

寶座廳的門再次開啟，一行紅衣主教走了出來，他們在秘密走廊中走過，一邊走一邊交談，他們都是身著紫色的老人，大多數都很虛弱，看上去也很疲憊。下一刻，牧師為羅馬進來了。

"The Holy Father will be ready to receive you presently," he said in a hushed and reverent whisper, and she rose to follow him.

"聖父很快就準備好接見你," 他以壓低而恭敬的聲音說道，於是她起身跟隨他。

A moment later Roma was at the door of the grand throne room. A chamberlain took charge of her there, and passed her to a secret chamberlain at the door of an anteroom adjoining. This secret chamberlain handed her on to a Monsignor in a violet cassock, and the Monsignor accompanied her to the door of the room in which the Pope was sitting.

片刻之後，羅馬來到了大寶座室的門前。一個侍衛在那裡接手她，並將她引導到與之相鄰的前室的門口的秘密侍衛處。這位秘密侍衛將她交給一位穿著紫色法衣的主教，並由主教陪同她走到教皇正在的房間的門口。

"As you approach," he said in a low tone, "you will make three genuflexions—one at the door, another midway across the floor, the third at the Holy Father's feet. You feel well?"

"當你接近時，"他低聲說，"你將做三次鞠躬：第一次在門口，第二次在地板的中間，第三次在聖父的腳前。你覺得良好嗎？"

"Yes," she faltered.

「是的，」她支吾了一句。

The door was opened, the Monsignor stepped one pace into the room, and then knelt and said—

門開了，主教走進房間一步，然後跪下來說-

"Donna Roma Volonna, your Holiness."

"羅馬伏洛那女士，你的神聖。"

Roma was on her knees at the threshold; a soft, full, kindly voice, which she could have believed she had heard before, called on her to approach; she rose and stepped forward, the Monsignor stepped back, and the door behind her was closed.

羅馬跪在門檻上;一個柔和、滿足、和藹的聲音叫她走近，她不禁認為她以前聽過這個聲音。她站起來邁步前進，樞機主教卻步後退，然後她身後的門關閉了。

She was in the Presence.

她在場。

III

The Pope, dressed wholly in white, was seated in a simple chair by a little table in a homely room, surrounded by bookcases and some busts of former pontiffs. There were little domesticities of intimate life about him, an empty soup-dish, a cruet-stand, a plate and a spoon. He had a face of great sweetness and spirituality, and as Roma approached he bent his head and smiled a fatherly smile. She knelt and kissed his ring, and continued to kneel by his chair, putting one hand on the arm. He placed his own mittened hand over hers and patted it tenderly, while he looked into her face.

教皇全身穿著白色的袍子，坐在一個簡單的椅子上，桌子旁邊是一個家常的房間，周圍是書櫃和一些前任教皇的半身像。他周圍有一些親密生活的小日常，如空的湯碗，調味品架，盤和湯匙。他有一張充滿甜美和靈性的臉，當羅馬走近時，他低頭並微笑著父親般的微笑。她跪下並親吻他的戒指，並繼續在他的椅子旁跪下，用一隻手放在扶手上。他將自己戴著手套的手放在她的手上，溫柔地拍拍，同時看著她的臉。

The little nervous perturbation with which Roma had entered the room began to leave her, and in the awful wearer of the threefold crown she saw nothing but a simple, loving human being. A feminine sense crept over her, a sense of nursing, almost of motherhood, and at that first moment she felt as if she wanted to do something for the gentle old man. Then he began to speak. His voice had that tone which comes to the voice of a man who has the sense of sex strong in him, when a woman is with him and his accents soften perceptibly.

當羅馬帶著一點小小的緊張進入房間時，這種感覺開始消失，而在這位三重皇冠的威嚴面容之下，她只看到了一個簡單而充滿愛的人。她覺得自己像個護士，幾乎到了母親的地步，那一刻她好像想要為這位溫和的老人做些什麼。然後他開始說話。他的聲音有著男性在女性面前，並且他的語調明顯變得柔和時所具有的那種感性的音調。

"My daughter," he said, "Father Pifferi has spoken about you, and by your permission, as I understand it, he has repeated the story you told him. You have suffered, and you have my sympathy. And though you are not among the number of my children, I sent for you, that, as an old man to a young woman, by God's grace I might strengthen you and support you."

"我的女兒，"他說，"皮菲瑞神父提起了您，且在您的許可下，他重述了您告訴他的故事。您曾遭受痛苦，我對此深感同情。雖然您並非我子女中的一員，我仍然打算見您，這是因為作為一名老人，我希望能借由上帝的恩典之下，支撐並堅強你。”

She kissed his ring again and continued to kneel by the arm of his chair.

她再次吻了他的戒指，並繼續跪在他的椅子旁邊。

"Long ago, my child, I knew one who was in something like the same position, and perhaps it is the memory of what befell that poor soul which impels me to speak to you.... But she is dead, her story is dead too; let time and nature cover them."

"很久以前，我的孩子，我知道一個處於類似情況的人，也許是我對那個可憐的靈魂所遭遇的事情的記憶促使我對你說話...但是她已經去世，她的故事也已經消亡;讓時間和自然覆蓋它們。"

His voice had a slight tremor. She looked up. There was a hush, a momentary thrill. Then he smiled again and patted her hand once more.

他的聲音微微顫抖。她抬起頭來。那時候有一種短暫的寧靜，瞬間的激動。然後他再次微笑，再次輕拍她的手。

"You must not let the world weaken you, my child, or cause you to doubt the validity of your marriage. Whether it is a good marriage, in effect as well as intention (one of you being still unbaptized), it is for the Church, not the world, to decide."

"你不能讓世界削弱你，我的孩子，或讓你對你的婚姻的有效性產生懷疑。無論這是一個好的婚姻，無論從實際還是意圖（你們中的一個仍未受洗），這都是由教會來決定的，而不是世界。"

Again Roma kissed the ring of the Pope, and again he patted the hand that lay under his.

"羅馬再一次吻了教皇的戒指，他再次輕拍躺在他下面的那隻手。"

"Nevertheless, there is something I wish you to do, my daughter," he said, in the same low tones. "I wish you to tell your husband."

"然而，我女兒，我還是希望你做一件事，"他低聲說，"我希望你告訴你的丈夫。"

"Holy Father," said Roma, "I have already told him. I had done so before I spoke to Father Pifferi, but only under the disguise of another woman's story."

"聖父，" 羅馬說，"我已經告訴他了。在我跟Pifferi神父對話之前，我已經在講述另一個女人的故事的偽裝下這樣做了。"

"And what did your husband say?"

"那麼，你的丈夫說了什麼？"

"He said what your Holiness says. He was very charitable and noble; so I took heart and told him everything."

"他說了你的聖潔所說的。他非常慷慨和高尚；所以我鼓起勇氣，告訴他所有的事情。"

"And what did he say then?"

"那他後來說了什麼呢？"

A cloud crossed her face. "Holy Father, he has not yet said anything."

雲彩掠過她的臉。"聖父，他還沒有說任何事呢。"

"Not anything?"

"什麼都沒有？"

"He is away; he has not replied to my letter."

"他不在；他沒有回覆我的信。"

"Has there been time?"

"有沒有時間？"

"More than time, your Holiness, but still I hear nothing."

"除了時間的流逝，您的聖潔，我仍然什麼都沒有聽到。"

"And what is your conclusion?"

"那麼，你的結論是什麼?"

"That my letter has awakened some pity, but now that he knows I am the wife I spoke about and he is the husband intended, he cannot forgive me as he said the husband would forgive, and his generous soul is in distress."

"我的信件引起了他的同情，但現在他知道了我就是我提到的那個妻子，他就是那個被提到的丈夫，他無法像他說的那樣原諒我，他那慷慨的心靈現在正感到痛苦。"

"My daughter, could you wish me to speak to him?"

"我的女兒，你希望我跟他說話嗎？"

The cloud fled from her face. "It is more than I deserve, far more, but if the Holy Father would do that...."

"雲從她的臉上飄然而去。 "這超出了我應得的，遠超出了，但如果神聖的父親願意那樣做...."

"Then I must know the names—you must tell me everything."

"那我必須知道名字 - 你必須告訴我一切。"

"Yes, yes!"

"是的，是的！"

"Who is your father, my child?"

"你的父親是誰，我的孩子？"

"My father died in banishment. He was a Liberal—he was Prince Prospero Volonna."

"我的父親在流放中去世。他是個自由主義者——他是普洛斯佩羅·沃隆納王子。"

"As I thought. Who was the other man?"

"正如我所想。那另一個男人是誰？"

"He was a distant kinsman of my father's, and I have lately discovered that he was the principal instrument in my father's deportation. He was my guardian, a Minister and a great man in Italy. It is the Baron Bonelli, your Holiness."

"他是我父親的遠房親戚，我最近發現他是我父親被驅逐出境的主要幕後推手。他曾是我的監護人，是義大利的一位部長和大人物。他就是您的聖人，那位奔奈利男爵。"

"Just so, just so!" said the Pope, tapping his foot in obvious heat. "But go on, my child. Who is your husband?"

“就是這樣，就是這樣！”教皇說，顯然有些焦躁地踏著腳。”但繼續，我的孩子。你的丈夫是誰？”

"My husband is a different kind of man altogether."

"我的丈夫完全是一種不同的人。"

"Ah!"

"啊！"

"He has done everything for me, Holy Father—everything. Heaven knows what I should have been now without him."

"他為我做了一切，聖父--一切事情。 上天知道，如果沒有他，我現在會變成什麼樣子。"

"God bless him! God bless both of you!"

"神保佑他！神保佑你們倆！"

"I came to know him by the strangest accident. He is a Liberal too, and a Deputy, and thinking of the corruptions of the Government, he pointed to me as the mistress of the Minister. It was not true, but I was degraded, and ... and I set out to destroy him."

"我透過最奇怪的意外認識了他。他也是一個自由主義者，並且是議員，在想到政府的腐敗時，他指我是部長的情婦。這不是事實，但我受到了侮辱，...我開始著手摧毀他。"

"A terrible vengeance, my child. Only the Minister could have thought of it."

"可怕的復仇，我的孩子。只有部長能想得出來。"

"Then I found that my enemy was one of my father's friends, and a true and noble man. Holy Father, I had begun in hate, but I could not hate him. The darkness faded away from my soul, and something bright and beautiful came in its place. I loved him, and he loved me. With all our hearts we loved each other."

"然後我發現我的敵人是我父親的朋友，且是一個真誠和高尚的人。神聖的父親，我是憎恨他開始的，但我無法恨他。黑暗從我的靈魂中消退，而某種明亮和美麗的東西取而代之。我愛他，他也愛我。我們全心全意地愛著彼此。"

"And then?"

"那麼呢?"

"Then he came back to me. I knew all the secrets I had set out to learn, but I could not give them up, and when I refused he threatened me."

"然後他回到了我身邊。我知道我要學習的所有秘密，但我不能放棄它們，當我拒絕時，他威脅我。"

"And what did you do?"

「你做了什麼？」

"I married my husband and withstood every temptation. It wasn't so very hard, for I cared nothing for wealth and luxury now. I only wanted to be good. God Himself should see how good I could be."

"我嫁給了我的丈夫，抵擋住了每一種誘惑。這並不太難，因為我現在對財富和奢侈生活並沒有任何興趣。我只想做一個好人。上帝自己應該看看我能有多麼善良。"

The Pope's eyes were moist. He was patting the young woman's trembling hand.

教宗的眼睛潤濕了。他輕輕地拍著那位年輕女子顫抖的手。

"My blessing rest on you, my daughter, and may the man you have married be worthy of your love and trust."

"願我的祝福降臨在你身上，我的女兒，願你所嫁之人配得上你的愛與信任。"

"Indeed, indeed he is," said Roma.

"確實，他確實是，" 羅馬說。

"He was your father's friend, you tell me?"

"他是你父親的朋友，是你告訴我的嗎？"

"Yes, your Holiness, and although we met again so recently, I had known him in England when I was a child."

"是的，您的神聖，儘管我們剛剛相見，但我在英國的時候就認識了他。"

"A Liberal, you say?"

"你說你是自由派？"

"Yes, your Holiness."

"是的，閣下的神聖。"

"The enmity of the Minister was the fruit of political warfare?"

"部長的敵意是政治鬥爭的果實?"

"Nothing but that at first, though now...."

"起初只是那樣，雖然現在...."

"I see, I see. And the secrets you speak of are only...."

"我明白，我明白。而你所說的秘密只是...."

"Only the doings of twenty years ago, which are dead and done with."

"只是二十年前的事，那些都已成為過去了。"

"Then your husband is older than you are?"

"那麼你的丈夫比你年長嗎？"

The young woman broke into a sunny smile, which set the Pope smiling.

那位年輕女子綻放出陽光般的笑容，這使得教皇也笑了起來。

"Only ten years older, your Holiness. He is thirty-four."

"神聖的，他只大我十歲。他今年34歲。"

"Where does he come from, and what was his father?"

"他來自哪裡，他的父親是誰？"

"He was born in Rome, but he does not know who his father was."

"他在羅馬出生，但他不知道他的父親是誰。"

"What is he like to look upon?"

"他看起來是什麼樣子的？"

"He is like ... I have never seen any one so like ... will your Holiness forgive me?"

"他就像...我從未見過如此相似的...請原諒我，您的聖潔嗎？"

The colour had mounted to her eyes, her two rows of pearly teeth seemed to be smiling, and the sunny old face of the Pope was smiling too.

顏色已經上升到她的眼睛，她的兩排珍珠般的牙齒似乎在笑，而教皇那陽光般的老臉也在笑。

"Say what you please, my daughter."

"隨你說，我的女兒。"

"I have never seen any one so like the Holy Father," she said softly.

"我從未見過有人如此像神聖的父親，"她輕聲說。

Her head was held down and there was a little nervous tremor at her heart. The Pope patted her hand affectionately.

她低下了頭，心中有一絲緊張的震動。教皇慈愛地拍了拍她的手。

"Have I asked you his name, my child?"

"我有問過你他的名字了嗎，我的孩子？"

"His name is David Rossi."

他的名字是大衛·羅西。

The Pope rose suddenly from his seat, and for the first time his face looked dark and troubled.

教皇突然從座位上站起來，他的臉色第一次顯得陰沉困憔。

"David Rossi?" he repeated in a husky voice.

"大衛·羅西？"他以嘶啞的聲音重複說。

Roma began to tremble. "Yes," she faltered.

"羅馬開始顫抖。"對，"她結結巴巴的說。

"David Rossi, the Revolutionary?"

"大衛·羅西，革命者？"

"Indeed no, your Holiness, he is not that."

"確實不是，您的神聖，他不是那個。"

"But, my child, my child, he is the founder of a revolutionary society which this very day the Holy Father has condemned."

"但是，我的孩子，我的孩子，他是一個革命社會的創始人，就在今天，教宗已經譴責了他。"

He walked across the room and she rose to her feet and looked after him.

他走過了房間，她站起來看著他的背影。

"One of the men who are conspiring against the peace of the Church—banded together to fight the Church and its head."

"有一些人聯合起來，陰謀破壞教會的和平-結盟對抗教會及其領袖。"

"Don't say that, your Holiness. He is religious, deeply religious, and far more an enemy of the Government and the King."

"不要這麼說，尊敬的聖偉。他是宗教的，深度的宗教，並且比政府和國王的敵人更多。"

She began to talk wildly, almost aimlessly, trying to defend Rossi at all costs.

她開始瘋狂地，幾乎無目的地說話，試圖不惜一切代價捍衛羅西。

"Holy Father," she said, "shall I tell you a secret? There is nobody else in the world to whom I could tell it, but I can tell it to you. My husband is now in England organising a great scheme among the exiles and refugees of Italy. What it is I don't know, but he has told me that it will lead to the conquest of the country and the downfall of the throne. Whether it is to be a conspiracy in the ordinary sense, or a constitutional plan of campaign, he has not said, but everything tells me that it is directed against the politics of Rome, and not against its religion, and is intended to overthrow the King, and not the Pope."

"聖父，"她說，"我可以告訴你一個秘密嗎？除了您，世界上沒有其他人我可以告訴了。我的丈夫現在在英國，在義大利的流亡者和難民中組織一個大型計劃。我不知道那是什麼，但他告訴我，這會導致對國家的征服和王位的垮臺。我不清楚是否將以普通意義上的陰謀，或是個憲法式的戰役計劃來進行，但所有事情告訴我，這是針對羅馬的政治，而不是其宗教，旨在推翻國王，而非教皇的。"

The Pope, who had been standing with his back to Roma, turned round to her with a look of fright. His eyebrows had met over the vertical lines on his forehead, and this further reminder of another face threw Roma into still greater confusion.

教宗一直背對著羅馬站著，他驚恐地轉過身來看著她。他的眉毛在他額頭的垂直線上相遇，這更多的提醒使羅馬陷入了更大的困惑。

"'When I come back, it will be with such a force behind me as will make the prisons open their doors and the thrones of tyrants tremble.' That's what he said, your Holiness. The movement will come soon, too, I am sure it will, and then your Holiness will see that, instead of being irreligious men, the leaders of the people...."

"'當我回來時，背後將有如此強大的力量，足以使監獄敞開大門，暴君的王座震顫。' 這就是他說的，您的聖潔。很快，運動就會來臨，我確信會的，然後您的聖潔將會看到，民眾的領導者，他們並非不敬神的人...."

The Pope held up his hand. "Stop!" he cried. "Say no more, my child. God knows what I must do with what you have said already."

教宗舉起手來。“停！”他喊道。“不要再說了，我的孩子。上帝知道我該怎麼處理你已經說過的話。”

Then Roma saw what she had done in the wild gust of her emotion, and in her terror she tried to take it back.

然後，羅馬看到她在情緒的狂風中做了什麼，並且在她的恐慌中，她試圖收回。

"Holy Father, you must not think from what I say that David Rossi is for revolution and regicide...."

"聖父，您絕不能從我所說的中認為大衛·羅西支援革命和篡位......"

"Don't speak, my child. You cannot know what an earthquake you have opened at my feet. Let me think!"

"不要說話，我的孩子。你不可能知道你在我腳下開啟了多大的地震。讓我想想！"

There was silence for a moment, and then Roma gulped down the great lumps in her throat and said: "I am only an ignorant woman, Holy Father, and perhaps I have said too much, and do not understand. But what I have told your Holiness was told me in love and confidence. And the Holy Father is wise and good, and whatever he does will be for the best."

片刻的寂靜過後，羅馬勉強壓下喉嚨中的大塊哽咽，然後她說：“我只是一個無知的女人，聖父，也許我說得太多，也不理解。但是我對您的聖認所說的都是別人憑愛與信任告訴我的。聖父是明智且善良的，他做的一切都將是最好的。”

The Pope returned to his chair with a bewildered look, and did not seem to hear. Roma sank to her knees by his side and said in a low, pleading tone:

教宗帶著困惑的神情返回到他的座位上，似乎沒有聽到。羅馬人跪在他的身邊，低聲懇求地說：

"My husband's faith in me is so beautiful, your Holiness. Oh, so beautiful. I am the only one in the world to whom he has told all his secrets, and if any of them should ever come back to him...."

"我的丈夫對我如此深信，您的聖潔。哦，太美妙了。我是世界上唯一一個他全部秘密都告訴過的人，如果有任何秘密被人揭穿回到他那裡...."

"Don't be afraid, my daughter. What you said in simple confidence shall be as sacred as if it had been spoken under the seal of the confessional."

"別怕，我的女兒。你所簡單地誠實表白的話，將會像在告解時誓言一樣神聖。"

"If I could tell your Holiness more about him—who he is and where he comes from—a place so lowly and humble, your Holiness...."

"如果我能告訴您的聖潔更多關於他的資訊——他是誰以及他從何處來——一個如此卑微和謙遜的地方，您的聖潔...."

"Tell me no more, my child. It is better I should not know. Pity ought to have no place in what duty tells me to do. But I can love David Rossi for all that. I do love him. I love him as a lost and wayward son, whose hand is raised against his Father, though he knows it not."

"不要再告訴我了，我的孩子。最好我不知道。同情應該在職責告訴我該做什麼的時候沒有位置。但是儘管如此，我能愛David Rossi。我確實愛他。我把他當作一個迷失和越軌的兒子愛著，他的手反抗他的父親，儘管他並不知道。"

There was a bell button on the Pope's chair. He pressed it, and the Participante returned to the room without knocking. The Pope rose and took Roma's hand.

教皇的座椅上有個鈴鐺按鈕。他按下它，參賽者沒有敲門就回到了房間。教皇站起來並握住了羅馬的手。

"Go in peace and with my blessing, my child. I bless you! May my fatherly blessing keep you pure in heart, may it strengthen you in all temptations, comfort you in all trials, avert from you every evil omen, and bring you into the fold of Christ's children at the last."

"去吧，我的孩子，在和平與我祝福的陪伴下。我祝福你！願我的父親的祝福讓你心淨如初，它能在所有的誘惑中堅固你，為你在所有困苦中帶來慰藉，為你避開所有的邪惡預兆，並在最後帶你進入基督的孩子團體。"

The Participante stepped forward and signed to Roma to withdraw. She rose and left the presence chamber, stepping backward and too much moved to speak. Not until the door had been closed did she realise that she was crossing the throne room, and that the Bussolante was walking beside her.

參加者向前走去，並且示意羅馬撤退。她起身離開了王座大廳，向後退去，感動得無法說話。直到門關閉，她才意識到她正在穿越王座房間，並且Bussolante正在她身邊行走。

IV

When the Pope walked in his garden that afternoon as usual, the old Capuchin was with him. From the door of the Vatican they drove in the Pope's landau with two of the Noble Guard riding beside the carriage, and one of the chamberlains walking behind it, through lanes enshrouded in laurel and ilex, until they reached the summer-house on the top of the hill. There the old men stepped down, the Pope in his white cassock, white overcoat and red hat, the Capuchin in his brown habit, skull-cap and sandals. The Pope's cat, a creature of reddish coat, which followed him into the garden as a dog follows his master, leapt out of the carriage after them.

當教宗那天下午像往常一樣在他的花園中散步時，與他同行的是一位老卡普奇諾修士。他們從梵蒂岡的門口乘坐教宗的馬車出發，兩名貴族衛隊騎士在馬車旁邊騎行，一名侍從在馬車後面走路，穿過被月桂和冬青環抱的小徑，直到他們到達山頂上的夏日小屋。然後老人們下車，教宗穿著他的白色長袍，白色大衣和紅帽，卡普奇諾修士穿著他的棕色長袍，頭巾和涼鞋。教宗的貓，一隻紅色的生物，跟隨他走進花園就像狗跟隨主人一樣，也從馬車後跳了出來。

The Pope was more than usually grave and silent. Once or twice the Capuchin said, "And how did you find my young penitent this morning?"

教皇今天比平時更加嚴肅而沉默。卡布奇諾神父一兩次問道：“今天早上你覺得我那年輕的懺悔者如何？”

"Bene, bene!" the Pope replied.

"好的，好的！"教皇回答。

But at length the Pope, scraping the gravel at his feet with the ferrule of his walking-stick, began to speak on his own initiative.

但最終，教皇開始主動發言，他用手杖的鐵箍刮著腳下的砂礫。

"Father!"

"父親!"

"Your Holiness?"

"尊貴的聖人?"

"The inscrutable decree of God which made me your Pontiff has not altered our relations to each other as men?"

"神秘的上帝旨意讓我成為你們的教皇，這並未改變我們作為人類之間的關係。"

The Capuchin took snuff and answered, "Your Holiness is always so good as to say so."

這個卡普錫恩修道士呷了一口煙，然後回答說，“陛下總是如此慈祥。”

"You are my master now just as you were thirty years ago, and there is something I wish to ask of you."

"你現在仍然是我的主人，就像三十年前一樣，我有些事想問你。"

"What is it, your Holiness?"

"尊敬的教宗，有什麼事嗎？"

"You have been a confessor many years, Father?"

"您當神父好多年了，對嗎？"

"Forty years, your Holiness."

"四十年，閣下的神聖。"

"In that time you have had many difficult cases?"

"在那段時間裡，你遇到了許多困難的案子嗎？"

"Very many."

"非常多。"

"Father, has it ever happened that a penitent, has revealed to you a conspiracy to commit a crime?"

"父親，有沒有過這樣的情況 - 一名懺悔者向你揭示了一個犯罪的陰謀?"

"More than once it has happened."

"這已經不止一次發生了。"

"And what have you done?"

"你做了什麼？"

"Persuaded him to reveal it to the civil authorities, or else tell it to me outside the confessional."

"說服他向公民當局揭示，或者在告解之外告訴我。"

"Has the penitent ever refused to do so?"

"悔罪者有沒有拒絕過這樣做？"

"Never."

"永不"

"But if ... if the case were such as made it difficult for the penitent to reveal the conspiracy to the civil authorities, having regard to the penalties the revelation would bring with it ... if by reason of ties of blood and affection such revelation were humanly impossible, and it would even be cruel to ask for it, what would you do then?"

"但如果...如果情況讓悔罪者難以向民事當局揭露陰謀，考慮到揭露會帶來的懲罰...如果由於血緣和感情的關係，這種揭露在人性上是不可能的，甚至要求它會是殘酷的，那您會怎麼做呢?"

"Nothing, your Holiness."

"沒有什麼，神聖的。"

"Not even if the crime to be committed were a serious one, and it touched you very nearly?"

"即使即將犯下的罪行是嚴重的，並且與你息息相關，你也不會介意嗎？"

The Capuchin shook out his coloured print handkerchief and said, "That could make no difference, your Holiness."

那個卡普奇諾修道士搖出他的彩色印花手帕，並說，“這不會有任何差別，閣下。”

"But suppose you heard in confession that your brother is to be assassinated, what is your duty?"

"但假設你在告解中聽到你的兄弟將要被暗殺，你的責任是什麼？”

"My duty to the penitent who reveals his soul to me is to preserve his secret."

"我對向我揭示靈魂的悔者的職責是保護他的秘密。"

"And what is your duty to God?"

"那麼，你對上帝的責任是什麼？"

The handkerchief dropped from the Capuchin's hand.

這頂手帕從Capuchin的手中掉了下來。

The Pope paused, scraped the gravel with the ferrule of his stick, and said:

教皇停下來，用他手杖的鐵環刮著砂石，然後說:

"Father, I am in the position of the confessor who has guilty knowledge of a conspiracy against the life of his enemy."

"父親，我就像知罪者一樣，對於一項針對他的敵人的陰謀有所知情。"

The Capuchin pushed his handkerchief into his sleeve and dropped back into his seat. After a moment the Pope told the story of what Roma had said of Rossi's plans abroad.

卡普其恩將手帕塞入袖子中，然後退回座位上。過了一會，教皇敘述了羅馬關於羅西在國外計劃的說法。

"A conspiracy," he said, "plainly a conspiracy."

"這明顯是一種陰謀，"他說。

"And what do you understand the conspiracy to be?"

"那你對陰謀的理解是什麼?"

"Who can say? Perhaps a recurrence to the custom of the Middle Ages, when citizens who had been banished by their opponents used to apply themselves in exile to attempt the reconquest of their country by stirring up the factions at home."

"誰能說得清楚？也許是回到中世紀的習慣，當時被對手驅逐的公民會在流亡中致力於試圖透過煽動國內的派系來重新徵服他們的國家。"

"You think that is Rossi's object?"

"你認為那是羅西的目標嗎？"

"I do."

"我願意。"

The Capuchin shifted uneasily the skull-cap on his crown and said:

這名Capuchin修士不安地在他的頂上擺動骷髏帽，他說：

"Holy Father, I trust your Holiness will leave the matter alone."

"聖父，我相信您的神聖會放下這件事。"

"Why so?"

"為什麼這樣?"

"In reading history I do not find that such enterprises have usually been successful. I see, rather, how commonly they have failed. And if it was so in the Middle Ages when the arts of war were primitive, how much less likely are the conspiracies of secret societies, the partial and superficial risings of refugees, to be serious now in the days of standing armies."

在閱讀歷史時，我並未發現此類事業通常能夠成功。相反，我看到它們多麼常常失敗。如果在戰爭藝術還處於原始狀態的中世紀，這種情況就已經如此，那麼在現今擁有常備軍隊的時代，秘密社團的陰謀、難民的部分和表面的起義又如何可能變得嚴重呢？

"True. But is that a good reason for doing nothing in this instance?"

"對。但這是在這種情況下什麼都不做的好理由嗎？"

"But, Holy Father, think. You cannot disclose the secrets this poor lady has revealed to you. Her confession was only a confidence, but your Holiness knows well that there is such a thing as a natural secret which it would be a great fault to reveal. Facts which of their own nature are confidential belong to this order. They are assimilated to the confessional, and as such they should be respected."

"但是，聖父，您得想想。您不能透露這位可憐的女士向您表露的秘密。她的告解只是一種信任，但是您的聖潔知道，自然界中有一種秘密，如果被揭示出來，那將是一個很大的錯誤。本質上具有保密性質的事實屬於此類。他們被視為口供，並因此應該得到尊重。"

"Indeed they should."

"確實他們應該。"

"Then it is not possible for your Holiness to reveal what you heard this morning without bringing trouble to the penitent and wronging her in relation to her husband."

"那麼，您的聖潔不可能揭示您今天早上聽到的事情，而不對悔罪者造成困擾，並對她和她的丈夫不公。"

"God forbid that I should do so, whatever happens. But is a priest forbidden to speak of a sin heard in confession if he can do so in such a way that the identity of the penitent cannot be discovered?"

"但願我不會這麼做，無論發生什麼事。但是，如果一個神父能以某種方式談論在告解中聽到的罪行，而又不會被發現是誰的懺悔者的身份，那麼他被禁止談論這種罪行嗎？"

"Your Holiness intends to do that?"

"您的聖潔打算那樣做嗎？"

"Why not?"

為什麼不呢？

"The Holy Father knows best. For my own part, your Holiness, I think it a danger to tamper with the secrets of a soul, whatever the good end in view or the evil to be prevented."

"聖父是最明智的。就我個人來說，您的聖潔，我認為揭開靈魂秘密是危險的，無論出於何種良好目的，或者要防止的惡行。"

The Capuchin looked round to where the horses were pawing the path and the Guards stood by the carriage.

這位卡普奇修士看向馬蹄踏踩小徑的地方，以及衛士們站在馬車旁的景象。

"Thirty-five years ago we had a terrible lesson in such dangers, your Holiness."

"三十五年前，我們在這樣的危險中經歷了一次可怕的教訓，您的聖潔。"

The Pope dropped his head and continued to scrape the gravel.

教皇低下頭，繼續在碎石上刨。

"Your Holiness remembers the poor young woman who told her confessor she was about to marry a rich young man. The confessor thought it his duty to tell the young man's father in general terms that such a marriage was to be contracted. What was the result? The marriage took place in secret and ended in grief and death."

"您的聖潔還記得那位貧窮的年輕女子對她的告解神父說，她即將嫁給一位富有的年輕男子。告解神父認為有責任向年輕男子的父親大致說明此類婚姻將要訂立。結果如何呢？這場婚禮秘密舉行，最終以悲劇和死亡作結。"

The Pope rose uneasily. "We will not speak of that. It was a case of a father's pride and perverted ambition. This is a different case altogether. A man who is a prey to diabolical illusions, an enemy of the Church and of social order, is hatching a plot which can only end in mischief and bloodshed. The Holy Father knows it. Shall he keep this guilty knowledge locked in his own bosom? God forbid!"

教宗不安地站了起來。"我們不談那件事。那只是一個父親的自豪和扭曲的野心。這是一種完全不同的情況。一個受惡魔幻覺影響的人，敵視教會和社會秩序，正在策劃一個只會以禍亂和流血告終的陰謀。神聖的教宗知道這一切。他應該將這個有罪的知識鎖在自己的胸膛裡嗎？絕不應該！"

"Then you intend to warn the civil authorities?"

"那你打算警告民事當局嗎？"

"I must. It is my duty. How could I lay my head on my pillow and not do it? But I will do it discreetly. I will commit no one, and this poor lady shall remain unknown."

"我必須這麼做，這是我的責任。我怎麼能躺在枕頭上而不去做呢？但我會謹慎地去做，我不會涉及任何人，這位可憐的女士將會不為人知。"

The venerable old men, each leaning on his stick, walked down a path lined by clipped yews, shaded by cypresses, and almost overgrown with crocus, anemone, and violet. Suddenly from the bushes there came a flutter of wings, followed by the scream of a bird, and in a moment the Pope's cat had leapt on to a marble which stood in the midst of the jungle. It was an ancient sarcophagus, placed there as a fountain, but the spring that had fed it was dry, and in its moss-grown mouth a bird had made its nest. The cat was about to pounce down on the eggs when the Pope laid hold of it.

`那些可敬的老人，每人都倚著他的柺杖，走下一個被修剪整齊的紫杉林夾道，由松柏遮蔽，幾乎被藏紅花，銀蓮花和紫羅蘭蔓延得滿目翠綠。突然，從叢中飛出一陣翅膀的撲撲聲，接著是一隻鳥的尖叫聲，瞬間，教皇的貓就跳到了叢林中央的一塊大理石上。那是一個古老的石棺，被當作噴泉放在那裡，但餵它的春水已經乾涸，鳥在其長滿苔蘚的口中築了巢。貓正要撲向鳥蛋，這時教皇抓住了它。`

"Ah, Meesh, Meesh," he said, "what an anarchist you are, to be sure!... Monsignor!"

"啊，米什，米什，"他說，"你確實是個無政府主義者！... 主教！"

"Yes, your Holiness," said the chamberlain, coming up behind.

"是的，聖潔的領袖，"侍從走上前來說。

"Take this gatto rosso back to the carriage, and keep him in domicilio coatto until we come."

"把這隻紅色的貓帶回馬車，並將它留在強制性住所，直到我們回來。"

The Monsignor laughed and carried off the cat, and the Pope put his mittened hand gently on the little speckled eggs.

教區長閣下笑了起來，帶走了那隻貓，而教皇則用他戴著手套的手輕輕地摸了摸那些小斑點的雞蛋。

"Poor things! they're warm. Listen! That's the mother bird screaming in the tree. Hark! She's watching us, and waiting for us to go. How snugly she thought she kept her secret."

"可憐的小東西！它們都是暖的。聽！那是樹上的母鳥在尖叫。聽著！她正在看著我們，等待我們離開。她多麼安心地以為她的秘密被保護得很好。"

The Capuchin drew a long breath. "Yes, nature has the same cry for fear in all her offspring."

這個加布洛雕像長長的吸了一口氣，說道："是的，自然之母對所有子女的恐懼吶喊是相同的。"

"True," said the Pope.

"確實如此，"教皇說。

"It makes me think of that poor girl this morning."

"這讓我想起今早那個可憐的女孩。"

The Pope walked back to the carriage without saying a word. As he returned to the Vatican, the Angelus was ringing from all the church bells of Rome, the city was bathed in crimson light, the sun was sinking behind Monte Mario, and the stone pines on the crest of the hill, standing out against the reddening sky, were like the roofless columns of a ruined temple.

教皇沒有說一句話就走回馬車。當他回到梵蒂岡時，羅馬的所有教堂鐘聲中都在響起天使誦讀的聲音，全城沐浴在深紅的光中，太陽正在蒙特·馬里奧山後面沉下，山頂上的石松，在泛紅的天空中突出，就像一座無頂的廢棄寺廟的柱子。

V

Next day Francesca came up with a letter. The porter from Trinità de' Monti had brought it and he was waiting below for a present. In a kind of momentary delirium Roma snatched at the envelope and emptied her purse into the old woman's hand.

隔天，弗朗西斯卡帶著一封信來了。這是特立尼塔山的門房送來的，他正在下面等待禮物。羅馬在一種短暫的狂熱中搶過信封，並將錢包裡的錢倒進了老婦人的手中。

"Santo Dio!" cried Francesca, "all this for a letter?"

"天哪！"弗朗西斯卡喊道，"所有這一切只是為了一封信嗎？"

"Never mind, godmother," said Roma. "Give the money to the good man and let him go."

"沒關係，教母，" 羅馬說。 "把錢給那好人，讓他走吧。"

"It's from Mr. Rossi, isn't it? Yes? I thought it was. You've only to say three Ave Marias when you wake in the morning and you get anything you want. I knew the Signora was dying for a letter, so...."

"這是來自羅西先生的，對吧？是的？我就知道是。你只需要在早上醒來時說三聲聖母瑪利亞經，你就能得到你想要的任何東西。我知道這位夫人正在渴望一封信，所以...."

"Yes, yes, but the poor man is waiting, and I must get on with my work, and...."

"是的，是的，但那位可憐的人在等待，我必須繼續我的工作，還有...."

"Work? Ah, Signora, in paradise you won't have to waste your time working. A lady like you will have violins and celestial bread and...."

"工作？啊，夫人，在天堂裡，您將不必浪費時間做這種事情。像您這樣的淑女將擁有小提琴和天上的麵包..."

"The man will be gone, godmother," said Roma, hustling the deaf old woman out of the room.

"那個男人將會離開，教母，" Roma說，一邊催促著這個耳聾的老女人離開房間。

But even when Roma was alone she could not at first find courage to open the envelope. There was a certain physical thrill in handling it, in turning it over, and in looking at the stamps and the postmark. The stamps were French and the postmark was of Paris. That fact brought a vague gleam of joy. Rossi had been travelling, and perhaps he had not yet received her letter.

但是，即使羅馬人獨自一人，她起初也沒有勇氣打開信封。在處理它、翻看它以及檢視郵票和郵戳時，有一種特定的身體震顫。郵票是法國的，郵戳是巴黎的。那個事實帶來了一絲模糊的喜悅。羅西一直在旅行，也許他還沒有收到她的信。

With a trembling kiss and a little choking prayer she broke the seal at last, and as the letter came rustling out of the envelope she glanced at the closing lines:

她帶著顫抖的親吻和些許哽咽的祈禱，終於破開了封印。當信件從信封中滑落出來時，她瞥了一眼結尾的幾行：

"Your Faithful Husband."

"你的忠誠丈夫。"

She caught her breath and waited a moment, tingling all over. Then she unfolded the paper and read:—

她屏住呼吸，等待片刻，全身充滿了興奮之感。然後，她展開了紙張，開始閱讀：—

"Dearest,—A telegram from Rome, published in the Paris newspapers this morning, reports the trial and death of Bruno. To say that I am shocked is to say little. I am shaken to my foundations. My heart is bursting and my hand can with difficulty hold the pen.

"親愛的，今早巴黎的報紙刊登了關於布魯諾在羅馬的審判和死亡的電報。說我震驚實在是言之不足。我從內心深處被震撼。我的心即將崩裂，手中的筆都無法正常握住。"

"The news first reached me last evening, when I was in a restaurant with a group of journalists. We were at dinner, but I was compelled to rise and return to my lodgings. I must have been almost in delirium the whole night long. More than once I started from my sleep with the certainty that I heard Bruno's voice calling to me. Once I went to the window and looked out into the silent street. And yet I knew all the time that my poor friend lay dead in prison.

"昨晚我在餐廳與一群記者吃晚餐時，首次獲得了這個消息，但我被迫起身並返回我的住所。昨晚我一定處於近乎發狂的狀態。我多次從睡夢中驚醒，確信我聽到布魯諾的聲音在叫我。有一次我走到窗邊，向寂靜的街道外望去。然而，我始終知道，我那可憐的朋友已經在監獄中去世了。"

"Poor Bruno! I do not hold with suicide under any circumstances. A man's life does not belong to himself. Each of us is a soldier, and no sentinel ought to kill himself at his post. Who knows what the next turn of the battle will be? It is our duty to the General to see the fight out. But when the sentinel dies rather than pass a false watchword, suicide is sacrifice, death is victory, and God takes His martyr under the wings of His mercy.

"可憐的布魯諾! 在任何情況下，我都不贊成自殺。人的生命並不屬於自己。我們每個人都是士兵，沒有哨兵應該在他的崗位上自殺。誰知道戰爭的下一轉會是什麼?我們有責任對將軍看完這場戰鬥。但是，當哨兵寧願死去，也不願意讓一個錯誤的口令通過，那麼自殺就是犧牲，死亡就是勝利，而上帝會把他的殉道者帶到他的慈悲之翅下。"

"The poor fellow died believing I had been false to him! I knew him for eight years, and during that time he was more faithful to me than my shadow. He was the bravest, staunchest friend man ever had. And now he has left me, thinking I have wronged him at the last. Oh, my brother, do you not know the truth at last? In the world to which you are gone, does no heavenly voice tell you? Does not death reveal everything? Can you not look down and see all, tearing away the veil that clouded your vision here below? Is it only vouchsafed to him who remains on earth to know that he was true to the love you bore him? God forbid it! It cannot, cannot be.

"那可憐的人死了，認為我對他不忠！我認識他八年，這期間他對我比我自己的影子還忠誠。他是人間最勇敢、最堅定的朋友。現在他離開了我，認為我在最後辜負了他。哦，我的兄弟，你是否最後知道了真相？在你去的那個世界裡，是否有天使向你揭示真相？死亡不是揭示了一切嗎？你不能從上面看下來，雲霾遮蔽的畫面不再，您能看清所有嗎？只有留在地球上的人才知道他對你的愛是真誠的嗎？上帝不會允許這樣！絕對不會的。"

"Dearest, I came to Paris unexpectedly ten days ago...."

"親愛的，我十天前意外地來到了巴黎...."

Roma lifted her swimming eyes. "Then he hasn't received it," she thought.

羅馬抬起她泳池般的眼睛。"那麼他還沒收到，"她想。

"Called in haste, not only to organise our Italian people for the new crusade, but to compose by a general principle the many groups of Frenchmen who, under different names, have the same aspirations—Marxists, Possibilists, Boulangists, Guesdists, and Central Revolutionists, with their varying propaganda, co-operative, trade-unionist, anti-semite, national, and I know not what—I had almost despaired of any union of interests so pitifully subdivided when the news of Bruno's death came like a trumpet-blast, and the walls of the social Jericho fell before it. Everybody feels that the moment of action has arrived, and what I thought would be an Italian movement is likely to become an international one. A great outrage on the spirit of Justice breaks down all barriers of race and nationality.

"我被急忙召集，不僅是為了組織我們的義大利人去進行新的十字軍東征，而且還需要用一種廣泛的原則來整合那些有著相同抱負但卻用不同名字來稱呼自己的法國人群體－ 馬克思主義者，可能主義者，布朗吉斯特，蓋斯德主義者和中央革命者，以及他們各自不同的宣傳方法，合作社，工會主義，反猶主義，民族主義，等等，我不知道還有什麼。當我幾乎絕望於這些如此痛苦地被細分的利益是否能統一時，布魯諾的死訊像喇叭般響亮，社會耶利哥的牆在它面前倒下。每個人都感覺到行動的時刻已經來臨，我原本以為會是一場義大利的運動，現在看來可能會變成一場國際的運動。一次對正義精神的巨大侮辱打破了所有種族和國籍的隔閡。"

"God guide us now. What did our Master say? 'The dagger of the conspirator is never so terrible as when sharpened on the tombstone of a martyr.' With all the heat of my own blood I tremble when I think what may be the effect of these tyrannies. Of course the ruling classes at home will wash their hands of this affair. When a Minister wants to play Macbeth he has no lack of grooms to dabble with Duncan's blood. But the people will make no nice distinctions. I wouldn't give two straws for the life of the King when this crime has touched the conscience of the people. He didn't do it? No, he does nothing, but he stands for all. Anarchists did not invent regicide. It has been used in all ages by people who think the spirit of Justice violated. And the names of some who practised it are written on marble monuments in letters of gold."

"願神指引我們。我們的主說了什麼？'密謀者的匕首在烈士的墓碑上磨利時，從未如此恐怖。'我思考這些暴行可能的影響時，我感到自己的血液熱烈而震顫。當然，國內的統治階級將對此事避而不談。當一位部長想要扮演馬克白時，並不缺乏想要塗抹鄧肯血液的僮僕。但人民將不會做出細微的區分。當這起罪行觸動了人民的良知時，我對國王的生命絲毫不放心。他沒做這件事？不，他什麼都沒做，但他代表了所有的事物。無政府主義者並沒有發明弒君。在所有的時代裡，認為正義之靈被侵犯的人都曾使用過它。並且其中一些實踐者的名字被黃金的字母刻在大理石的碑文上。"

Roma began to tremble. Had the Pope been right after all? Was it really revolution and regicide which Rossi contemplated?

"羅馬開始搖晃。教宗是否真的說對了?羅西真的在考慮革命和弒君嗎?"

"Dearest, don't think that because I am so moved by all this that other and dearer things are not with me always. Never a day or an hour passes but my heart speaks to you as if you could answer. I have been anxious at not hearing from you for ten days, although I left my Paris address in London for your letters to be sent on. Sometimes I think my enemies may be tormenting you, and then I blame myself for not bringing you with me, in spite of every disadvantage. Sometimes I think you may be ill, and then I have an impulse to take the first train and fly back to Rome. I know I cannot be with you always, but this absence is cruel. Happily it will soon be over, and we shall see an end of all sadness. Don't suffer for me. Don't let my cares distress you. Whatever happens, nothing can divide us, because love has united our hearts for ever.

"親愛的，不要因為我對所有這些事情感到如此動容，就認為我心中的其他更親密的事情已經不在了。從來沒有一天或一個小時過去，但我的心都在跟你說話，好像你能回答一樣。我已經十天沒有收到你的消息了，雖然我在倫敦留下了我的巴黎地址，讓你的信直接寄來。有時我覺得我的敵人可能在折磨你，那麼我就會因為沒有帶你跟我一起而自責，儘管有每一個不利的狀況。有時我認為你可能病了，那麼我有急切的衝動要搭第一個火車立刻回羅馬。我知道我不能總是和你在一起，但這個缺席是殘酷的。幸運的是，它很快就會結束，我們將看到所有悲傷的終結。不要為我受苦。不要讓我的煩惱困擾你。無論發生什麼事，沒有什麼可以分開我們，因為愛情已經永遠地將我們的心結合在一起。"

"That's why I'm sure of you, Roma, sure of your love and sure of your loyalty. Otherwise how could I stay an hour longer after this awful event, tortured by the fear of a double martyrdom—the martyrdom of myself and of the one who is dearest to me in the world?

"這就是為什麼我對你有信心，羅馬，確信你的愛，確信你的忠誠。否則，在這悲劇事情後，我怎麼可能多待一個小時，被雙重殉道的恐懼所折磨——我自己的殉道和我在這世上最親愛的人的殉道?"

"The spring is coming to take me home to you, darling. Don't you smell the violets? Adieu!

"春天正要帶我回到你的身邊，親愛的。你沒聞到紫羅蘭的香氣嗎？再見！"

"Your Faithful Husband."

"你的忠實丈夫。"

Roma slept little that night. Joy, relief, disappointment, but, above all, fear for Rossi, apprehension about his plans, and overpowering dread of the consequences kept her awake for hours. Early next day a man in a blue uniform brought a letter from the Braschi Palace. It ran:—

羅馬那夜幾乎沒有睡眠。她因為對羅西的恐懼，對他計劃的擔憂，以及對結果的巨大恐懼而難以入睡，而喜悅、釋然、失望的情緒也充斥在她心頭。次日一早，一名著藍色制服的男子從Braschi宮殿帶來一封信，信上寫道:——

"Dear Roma,—I must ask you to come across to my office this morning, and as soon as convenient. You will not hesitate to do so when I tell you that by this friendly message I am saving you the humiliation of a summons from the police. Yours, as always, affectionately,

"親愛的羅馬，我必須請求你今天早上方便的時候來我辦公室一趟。當我告訴你，透過這條友善的消息，我正在為你省去由警方傳喚的羞辱，你將會毫不猶豫地這麼做。永遠親愛的就是你，"

Bonelli."

「邦內利。」

VI

The Minister of the Interior sat in his cabinet before a table covered with blue-books and the square sheets of his "projects of law," and the Commendatore Angelelli, with his usual extravagant politeness, was standing and bowing by his side.

內政部長坐在他的辦公室裡，面前的桌子上擺滿了藍皮書和他的"法律計畫"的方形紙張。而Commendatore Angelelli則以他那慣常的過分禮貌站在他身旁，恭恭敬敬地鞠躬。

"And what is this about proclamations issued by Rossi?" said the Baron, fixing his eye-glasses and looking up.

"羅西發出的這些公告是什麼意思？"男爵說著，扶正了他的眼鏡並抬頭看去。

"We have traced the printer who published them," said Angelelli. "After he was arrested he gave the name of the person who paid him and provided the copy."

"我們已經追蹤到那個出版它們的印刷商，" 安吉萊利說。"他被捕後，他提供了支付他並提供副本的人的名字。"

The Baron bowed without speaking.

男爵默默鞠躬。

"It was a certain lady, Excellency," said Angelelli in his thin voice, "so we thought it well to wait for your instructions."

"當然是一位貴婦人，閣下，"Angelelli用他的細聲說， "所以我們認為最好等待您的指示。"

"You did right, Commendatore. Leave that part of the matter to me. And Rossi himself—he is still in England?"

"您做的對，指揮官。將這部分的事情交給我。還有羅西他自己 - 他還在英國嗎？"

"In France, your Excellency, but we have letters from both London and Paris detailing all his movements."

"在法國，閣下，但我們有來自倫敦和巴黎的信件，詳細描述了他的所有行動。"

"Good."

"好的。"

"The Chief Commissioner writes that during his stay in London Rossi lodged in Soho, and received visits from nearly all the representatives of revolutionary parties. Apparently he united many conflicting forces, and not only the Democratic Federations and the Socialist and Labour Leagues, but also the Radical organisations and various religious guilds and unions gathered about him."

"首席專員寫道，羅西在倫敦逗留期間，他在蘇豪區的寓所接待了幾乎所有革命黨派的代表。顯然，他整合了許多矛盾的力量，不僅僅是民主聯盟和社會主義及工人聯盟，甚至還有激進組織和各種宗教公會和工會都圍繞在他身旁。"

The Baron made a gesture of impatience. "It's a case of birds of a feather. London has always been the central home of anarchy under various big surnames. What does the Commissioner understand to be Rossi's plan?"

男爵露出不耐煩的神情。他說：“這是物以類聚的情況。倫敦一直都是各種大名鼎鼎的無政府主義者的中心家園。警司認為羅西的計劃是什麼？”

"Rossi's plan, the Commissioner thinks, is to send back the Italian exiles, and to disperse them, with money and literature gathered abroad, among the excited millions at home."

"總監認為，羅西的計劃是將流亡的義大利人送回，並將他們用在國外收集的錢財和文獻分散在家鄉的激動人心的百萬群眾中。"

"Wonderful!" said the Baron.

"太棒了!"男爵說。

Angelelli laughed his thin laugh, like a hen cackling over its nest. Then he said:

"Angelelli發出他細薄的笑聲，就像一隻母雞在巢裡咯咯地笑。 然後他說："

"But the Prefect of Paris has formed a more serious opinion, your Excellency."

"但是，巴黎警視對此有更嚴重的看法，尊敬的閣下。"

"What is it?"

"這是什麼?"

"That Rossi is conspiring to assassinate the King."

"那個羅西正在策劃刺殺國王。"

The Baron blinked the glasses from his nose and sat upright.

男爵從鼻子上一眨眼鏡片就掉下來，然後坐直身體。

"Apparently he was having less success in Paris, where the moral plea has been overdone, when reports of the Rocco incident...."

"顯然他在巴黎的成功並不如前，那裡的道德呼籲已經被過度強調，就在羅科事件的報告傳出時...."

"A most unlucky affair, Commendatore."

"這真是一場最不幸的事情，指揮官。"

"Meeting at cafés in order to avoid the control of the police ... In short, although he has no exact information, the Prefect warns us to keep double guard over the person of his Majesty."

"在咖啡館會面以避免警察的控制...總的來看，雖然他沒有確切的資訊，但是警察局長警告我們要對他的陛下進行雙重保護。"

The Baron rose and perambulated the hearthrug. "A pretty century, truly, for fools who pass for wise men, and for weaklings who threaten when the distance is great enough!... Commendatore, have you mentioned this matter to anybody else?"

男爵站起來，在壁爐地毯上走來走去。 "真是個美好的世紀，對於那些被視為智者的愚人，和對於足夠遠就會威脅的弱者來說！...貴族，你有跟其他人談過這件事情嗎?"

"To nobody whatever, Excellency."

"對任何人都不是，閣下。"

"Then think no more about it. It's nothing. The public mind must not be alarmed. Tighten the cord about our man in Paris. Adieu!"

"那就不要再想了。這沒有什麼。公眾的心不必被驚動。緊盯著我們在巴黎的那個人。再見!"

The Baron's next visitor was the Prefect of the Province, who looked more solemn and soldierly than ever.

男爵的下一位訪客是省長，他比以往看起來更加嚴肅和戰士般。

"Senator," said the Baron, "I sent for you to say that the Council has determined to put an end to the state of siege."

"參議員，"男爵說，"我召喚你來是想告訴你，議會已決定結束這個處於圍城狀態的情況。"

The Prefect bowed again severely.

「總督再次嚴肅地鞠躬。」

"The insurrection has been suppressed, the city is quiet, and the severities of military rule begin to oppress the people."

"起義已經被鎮壓，城市回復了平靜，但軍事統治的嚴格開始壓迫人民。"

The Prefect bowed again and assented.

"縣長再次鞠躬並表示同意。"

"The Council has also resolved, dear Senator, that the country shall celebrate the anniversary of the King's accession with general rejoicings."

"親愛的參議員，議會也已決定，我們的國家將以全民共慶的方式慶祝國王繼位的週年紀念。"

"Excellent idea, sir," said the Prefect. "To wipe out the depression of the late unhappy times by a public festival is excellent policy. But the time is short."

"非常好的想法，先生，"警察局長說。"透過公共節日來消除最近不幸時期的壓抑情緒是非常好的政策。但是時間非常短。"

"Very short. The anniversary falls on Easter Monday. That is to say, a week from to-day. You will therefore take the matter in hand immediately and push it on without further delay. The details we will discuss later, and arrange all programmes of presentations and processions. Meantime I have written a proclamation announcing the event. Here it is. You can take it with you."

"非常簡短。紀念日正好是復活節星期一。也就是說，就在今天一週之後。因此，你將馬上開始處理這件事，並毫不拖延地推進。我們將在稍後討論詳情並安排所有禮品的程序和遊行。同時我已經寫了一篇宣告以公告這件事。這就是它。你可以帶著它走。"

"Good!"

"好!"

"The King will also sign a decree of amnesty to all the authors and accomplices of the late acts and attempts at rebellion who were not the organising and directing minds. That is also written. Here it is. But his Majesty has not yet signed it."

"國王也將簽署一項赦免所有最近反叛行為的作者和同謀者的特赦令，只要他們不是組織和指導者。這也寫在這裡。但是陛下還尚未簽署。"

The Prefect took a second paper from the Baron's hand, glanced his eyes over it, and read certain passages. "'Seeing that on a day of public rejoicing we could not restrain an emotion of grief ... turning a pitying eye upon the inexperienced youths drawn into a vortex of political disorder ... we therefore decree and command the following acts of sovereign clemency....' May I expect to receive this in the course of the day, your Excellency?"

"總督從男爵手中接過第二個檔案,掃過眼前後,閱讀了其中的一些段落。'看到在公眾歡慶的日子裡,我們不能抑制悲痛的情感...用憐憫的眼光看著那些無經驗的青年被捲入政治混亂的漩渦...因此我們頒布並命令以下的主權寬恕的行為...' 我可以期待在今天之內收到這個，陛下嗎？"

"Yes. And now for your own part of the enterprise, dear Senator. You will order all mayors of towns to assemble in Rome to complete the preparations. You will arrange a procession to the Quirinal, when the people will call the King on to the balcony and sing the National Hymn. You will order banners to be made bearing suitable watchwords, such as 'Long live the King,' 'May he govern as well as reign,' 'Long live the Crown,' the 'Flag,' and (perhaps) the 'Army.' You will oppose these generating ideas to 'Atheism' and 'Anarchy.' The essential point is that the people must be caused by festivals, songs, bands of music, and processions to think of the throne as their bulwark and the King as their saviour, and to take advantage of every opportunity to attest their gratitude to both. You follow me?"

"是的。現在輪到您自己的部分了，親愛的參議員。您將命令所有城長集結在羅馬，完成準備工作。您將安排一場到奎利諾台的遊行，當人們呼喚國王走到陽臺上，並演唱國歌。您將命令製作帶有適當口號的橫幅，如'國王萬歲'，'願他既要執政也要統治'，'皇冠萬歲'，'旗幟'，和（也許）'軍隊'。您將這些生成的想法與'無神論'和'無政府狀態'相對。重要的是，人們必須透過節日，歌曲，樂隊和遊行來將王座視為他們的屏障，並將國王視為他們的救世主，並趁每一個機會來表達他們對這兩者的感激之情。你跟得上我嗎？"

"Perfectly."

"完美無瑕。"

"Then lose no time, Senator.... One moment."

那就別浪費時間了，參議員....等一下。

The Prefect had risen and reached the door.

警察局長已經站起來並走到了門口。

"If you can double the King's guard and change the company every day until the festival is over...."

"如果你能加倍國王的衛兵，並每天更換陣容，直到節日結束...."

"Easily, your Excellency. But wait; the Vatican Chief of Police has asked for help on Holy Thursday."

"輕松一點，閣下。但等一下; 教廷警察局長已經在聖週四尋求了幫助。"

"Give it him. Let the timid old man of the Sacred College have no excuse for saying we take more care of the King than of the Pope."

"把它給他。讓神聖學院的膽小的老人沒有藉口說我們比對教皇更關心國王。"

The Minister of Justice was the next of the Baron's visitors. He was a short man with a smiling and rubicund face, and he wore yellow kid gloves.

`接下來到訪男爵的是司法部長。這位部長是個矮矮的男子，臉上帶著微笑和紅潤的光芒，他戴著黃色的小羔羊皮手套。`

"All goes well and wisdom is justified of her children," said the Baron, rising again and promenading the hearthrug. "The national sentiment, dear colleague, is a sword, and either we must use it on behalf of the Government and the King, or stand by and see it used by the hostile factions."

"一切都進行得很順利，智慧由她的孩子們證明，"男爵說著再次站起來，在壁爐地毯上散步。"親愛的同事，國家情感就是一把劍，我們必須代表政府和國王使用它，否則就只能站在一旁，看著它被敵對派系使用。"

"Men like Rossi are not slow to use it, sir," said the little Minister.

"像羅西這樣的人，先生，不會緩慢地使用它," 小牧師說。

"Tut! It's not Rossi I'm thinking of now. It's the Church, the clergy, rich in money and in the faith of the populace. That's why I wanted to do something as set-off against those mourning demonstrations which the Pope has appointed."

"嘖！我現在想的不是羅西。我在想的是教會，牧師，他們擁有財富和人民的信仰。這就是我想要對抗那些由教宗指定的悼念活動而做些事情的原因。"

"Yes, the old gentleman of the Vatican knows the instincts and cravings of our people, doesn't he, sir? He knows they like a show, and the seasoning of their pleasures with a little religion."

"是的，梵蒂岡的那位老紳士知道我們人民的本能和渴望，不是嗎，先生？他知道他們喜歡看表演，並在他們的樂趣中加入一點宗教調味料。"

"It's the rustiest old weapon in the Pope's arsenal, dear colleague, but it may serve unless we do something. If the people can be persuaded that the Pope is their one friend in adversity, there couldn't be a better feather in the Papal cap. Happily our people love to sing and to dance as well as to weep and to pray. So we needn't throw up the sponge yet."

"這是教皇武器庫裡最老舊的武器，親愛的同事，但除非我們做些什麼，否則它也許還能派上用場。如果人們能被說服教皇是他們在逆境中的唯一朋友，那麼沒有比這更適合作為教皇帽的羽毛了。幸好我們的人民喜愛唱歌和跳舞，也喜歡哭泣和禱告。所以我們還不需要放棄。"

Both laughed, and the little Minister said, "Besides, it is so easy to change religious processions into political ones. And then the Vatican is always intriguing with the powers of rebellion and preaching obedience to the Pope alone."

兩人都笑了，然後小牧師說：“此外，將宗教遊行變成政治遊行是如此的容易。而且，梵蒂岡總是與反叛勢力密謀，並唯一呼籲人們服從教皇。”

The creaking of the Baron's patent-leather boots stopped, and he drew up before his colleague.

男爵的專利皮靴的吱吱聲停了下來，他停在他的同事面前。

"Watch that sharply," he said, "and if you see any sign on the part of the Vatican of intriguing with men like Rossi, any complicity with conspiracy, or any knowledge of plots pointing to revolution and regicide, let the Council hear of it immediately."

"小心觀察，"他說，"如果你看到梵蒂岡和像羅西這樣的人勾結的任何跡象，與陰謀有任何合謀，或知道任何可能指向革命和弒君的陰謀，立即通知理事會。"

The Baron's face had suddenly whitened with passion, and his little colleague looked at him in alarm. A secretary entered the room and handed the Baron a card. The Baron fixed his eye-glasses and read: "Monsignor Mario, Cameriere Segreto Partecipante di Sua Santità Pio X. Vaticano."

伯爵的臉色因為激動而突然變白，他的小夥伴驚恐地看著他。一位秘書走進房間，遞給伯爵一張卡片。伯爵調整了眼鏡，閱讀到：“教宗庇護十世的秘密參與者，Mario Monsignor。梵蒂岡。”

"St. Anthony! Talk of the angels...." muttered the little Minister.

“聖安東尼！談論天使...." 小教士嘀咕道。

"Will you perhaps...."

"你是否可能...."

"Certainly," said the Minister, and he left the room.

"當然，"部長說，然後他離開了房間。

"Show the Monsignor in," said the Baron.

「請讓主教進來，」男爵說。

VII

The Monsignor was young, tall, slight, almost fragile, and had thin black hair and large spiritual eyes. As he entered in the long black overcoat, which covered his cassock, he bowed and looked slowly round the room. His subdued expression was that of a sheep going through a gate where the dogs may be, and his manner suggested that he would fly at the first alarm.

這位神父年輕，高大，瘦弱，近乎虛弱，並有著薄薄的黑髮和極大的靈性眼神。他身披長黑風衣覆蓋著他的僧袍進入，當他進入時，他鞠躬並慢慢地繞著房間看。他壓抑的表情就像是一頭穿過可能有狗的門關的羊，他的舉止讓人覺得他會在第一次警報時逃跑。

The Baron looked over his eye-glasses and measured his man in a moment. "Pray sit," he said, and at the next moment the young Monsignor and the Baron were seated at opposite sides of the table.

男爵透過他的眼鏡看過去，一瞬間就評估出了對方。 “請坐，”他說，下一刻年輕的主教和男爵就坐在桌子的對面了。

"I am sent to you by a venerable and illustrious personage...."

"我是由一位可敬和傑出的人物派來找您的...."

"Let us say the Pope," said the Baron.

"讓我們說是教皇,"男爵說。

The young Monsignor bowed and continued, "to offer on his behalf a word of counsel and of warning."

那位年輕的樞機神父鞠躬並繼續說，“躬代他人訴之一言，給予忠告和警告。”

"It is an unusual and distinguished honour," said the Baron.

“這是一種不同尋常且卓越的榮譽，”男爵說道。

"I am instructed to inform you that the Holy Father has reason to believe a further and more serious insurrection is preparing, and to warn you to take the necessary steps to secure public order and to prevent bloodshed."

"我被指示通知你，教宗有理由相信更嚴重的叛亂正在醞釀之中，並警告你採取必要的措施來維持公共秩序，防止流血衝突。"

The Baron did not move a muscle. "If the Holy Father has special knowledge of a plot that is impending...."

"男爵一動不動。他說：“如果教皇對即將發生的陰謀有特殊的瞭解…"

"Not special, only general, but sufficient to enable him to tell you to hold yourself in readiness."

"不特殊，只是一般，但足以讓他告訴你要隨時準備好。"

"How long has the Holy Father been aware of this?"

"教宗知道這件事有多久了？"

"Not long. In fact, only since yesterday morning," said the Monsignor, and fearing he had said too much he added, "I only mention this to show you that the Holy Father has lost no time."

"不久。實際上，只是從昨天早上開始，"樞機主教說，他擔心自己說得太多，所以他又說，"我只是提這個讓你知道，教宗沒有浪費任何時間。"

"But if the Holy Father knows that a conspiracy is afoot, he can no doubt help us to further information."

"但如果教宗知道有陰謀正在進行，他無疑可以幫助我們獲得更多的資訊。"

The Monsignor shook his head.

樞機主教搖了搖頭。

"You mean that he will not do so?"

"你的意思是他不會這麼做嗎？"

"No."

"不"

"Am I, then, to understand that the information with which his Holiness honours me came to him secretly?"

"那我是否可以理解為，他的聖潔向我提供的資訊是秘密地傳給他的？"

"Yes, sir, secretly, and it is, therefore, not open to further explanation."

"是的，先生，這是秘密的，因此，不再需要進一步的解釋。"

"So it reached him by the medium of the confessional?"

"所以它是透過告解的方式傳達給他的嗎？"

The Monsignor rose from his seat. "Your Excellency cannot be in earnest."

"主教從座位上起身。他說：“尊敬的主教，你不可能是認真的。”"

"You mean that it did not reach him by the medium of the confessional?"

"你的意思是，這件事並非透過告解的方式傳達給他的嗎？"

"Certainly not."

"當然不是。"

"Then he is able to tell me everything, if he will?"

"那麼如果他願意，他能告訴我所有的事情嗎？"

The Monsignor became agitated. "The Holy Father's information came through a channel that is assimilated to the confessional, and is almost as sacred and inviolate."

"主教顯得焦慮。他說：'教皇的資訊來源被視為懺悔之道，幾乎同樣神聖，不可侵犯。'"

"But obedience to the Pope obliterates from all other responsibility. His Holiness has only to say 'Speak,' and his faithful child must obey."

"但對教皇的服從會消除所有其他的責任。只要他的聖潔說'說'，他的忠實孩子就必須服從。"

The Monsignor became confused. "His informant is not even a Catholic, and he has, therefore, no right to command her."

"主教變得困惑。「他的線人甚至不是天主教徒，因此，他沒有權力指揮她。」"

"So it is a woman," said the Baron, and the young ecclesiastic dropped his head.

"所以這是一個女人，"男爵說，年輕的神職人員低下了頭。

"It is a woman and a non-Catholic, and she visited the Holy Father at the Vatican yesterday morning; is that so?"

"這是一位非天主教的女士，她昨天上午拜訪了教宗在梵蒂岡的聖座，對嗎？"

"I do not assert it, sir, and I do not deny it."

"我並不是在斷定，先生，也不是在否認。"

The Baron did not speak for a moment, but he looked steadily over his eye-glasses at the flushed young face before him. Then he said in a quiet tone:

"男爵有一會兒沒說話，但他一直透過他的眼鏡定定地看著他面前那張激動的年輕面孔。然後他用平靜的語氣說:"

"Monsignor, the relations of the Pope and the Government are delicate, and if anything occurred to carry the disagreement further it might result in a serious fratricidal struggle."

"教宗大人，教宗和政府的關係是微妙的，如果發生任何事情使爭議進一步加劇，可能將導致嚴重的兄弟相爭。"

The Monsignor was trying to regain his self-possession, and he remained silent.

"主教正在試圖恢復他的鎮定，他保持沉默。"

"But whatever those relations, it cannot be the wish of the Holy Father to cover with his mantle the upsetters of order who are cutting at the roots of the Church as well as the State."

"但不論那些關係如何，教皇的願望絕不可能是用他的斗篷保護那些破壞秩序、既砍斷教會根因又顛覆國家的人。"

"Therefore I am here now, sir, thus early and thus openly," said the Monsignor.

"因此，我現在就在這裡了，先生，這麼早就這麼開放地在這裡了，"主教說。

"Monsignor," said the Baron, "if anything should occur to—for example—the person of the King, it cannot be the wish of his Holiness that anybody—myself, for instance—should be in a position to say to Parliament and to the Governments of Europe, 'The Pope knew everything beforehand, and therefore, not having revealed the particulars of the plot, the venerable Father of the Vatican is an accomplice of murderers.'"

"男爵對樞機主教說，'如果有任何事情發生在——例如——國王的身上，我認為教宗的意願絕不能是讓任何人——例如我——在議會和歐洲政府面前說出，'教宗事先已知道所有的事情，但因為沒有透露陰謀的所有細節，故此梵蒂岡的尊敬之父其實是兇手的同謀。'"

The young ecclesiastic lost himself utterly. "The Pope," he said, "knows nothing more than I have told you."

那位年輕的教士完全迷失了自己。他說：“教皇所知無過於我告訴你的。”

"Yes, Monsignor, the Pope knows one thing more. He knows who was his informant and authority. It is necessary that the Government should know that also, in order that it may judge for itself of the nature of the conspiracy and the source from which it may be expected."

"是的，主教，教皇有知道一件事情。他知道誰是他的消息提供者和權威。政府也需要知道這件事，以便他們可以自己判定這個陰謀的性質以及可能期待的來源。"
